لا؟ ولم أر نقلاً صريحاً فيها، وظاهر ما في الخانية من الشرب أن الحق يقبل الإسقاط أنه يسقط حقه فإنه صرح بأن حق الغانم قبل القسمة وحق المسيل المجرد وحق الموصى له بالسكنى وحق الموصى له بالثلث قبل القسمة وحق الوارث قبل القسمة يسقط . وصرح في جامع الفصولين من الفصل الثامن والعشرين : لو قال وارث تركت حقي لا يبطل حقه إذ الملك لا يبطل بالترك والحق يبطل به حتى لو أن أحد الغانمين قال قبل القسمة تركت حقي بطل حقه وكذا لو قال المرتهن تركت حقي في حبس الرهن يبطل اهـ. فقوله «والحق يبطل به يدل على ما ذكرنا فإن قلت : ذكر في الخانية. من كتاب الشهادات من كان فقيراً من أصحاب المدرسة يكون مستحقاً للوقف استحقاقاً لا يبطل بإبطاله فإنه لو قال أبطلت حقي كان له أن يطلب ويأخذ بعد ذلك اهـ . قلت : بينهما فرق لأن كلامنا فيما إذا كان الحق لمعين أسقطه، وأما ما في الخانية من الشهادات فالحق لغير معين فإنه وقف مطلق على فقراء المدرسة وغير المعين لا يصح إبطاله، وإنما خرج عن هذا الأصل ما إذا لم يكن الحق لمعين ومثله في الهبة. قال في البزازية : لو قال الواهب أسقطت حقي في الرجوع في الهبة لا يسقط اهـ . فإن قلت : إذا قال من له الشرط لا حق لي فيها ولا استحقاق ولا دعوى فهل له ولاية الإدخال والإخراج مع شرط الواقف؟ قلت : ليس له ذلك لكونه مقراً بأنه لا حق له وهو مؤاخذ بإقراره ولذا قال الخصاف لو وقف على ولده فأقر بأنه عليه وعلى زيد عمل بإقراره ما دام حياً حملاً على أن الواقف رجع عن اختصاصه وأشرك زيداً إلى آخره. وعلى معه الرملي وبدون هذا الشرط لا يطلق له ذلك قوله : وظاهر ما في الخانية من الشرب الخ) يستفاد منه الجواب عن الأولى والثانية وقوله وظاهر قوله في فتح القدير «الخ يستفاد منه الجواب عن الرابعة وبقي التوقف في الثالثة ولذا قال بعده ولم يظهر لي وجه الثالثة قوله : (وكذا لو قال المرتهن تركت حقي الخ) قال الرملي : سيأتي في هذا الشرح في باب من تقبل شهادته ومن لا تقبل في شرح قوله والشريك لشريكه بعد تقدم كلام فالحق أن . من أسقط حقه في وظيفة تقرر فيها أنه يسقط حقه فراجعه إن شئت قوله : (فيما إذا كان الحق لمعين أسقطه ظاهر هذا بل صريحه أن الموقوف عليه هذا سئلت فيمن له الإدخال والإخراج كلما بدا له فأدخل إنساناً فما الحيلة في عدم جواز إخراجه؟ فأجبت بأنه يقر بأنه لا حق له في إخراجه ولا تمسك له بما في شرط الواقف فلا يقدر على إخراجه بعده هذا ما ظهر لي والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم. وظاهر قوله في فتح القدير أن مسألة شرط الإدخال والإخراج إلى آخره على وزان مسألة الاستبدال أن للواقف الانفراد وليس للآخر الانفراد لما ذكرناه عن الخانية في مسألة ما إذا شرط الاستبدال لنفسه ولفلان معللاً بأن الواقف هو الذي شرط لذلك الرجل وما شرط لغيره فهو مشروط لنفسه اهـ. وقد يقال : لا فائدة حينئذ في اشتراطه معه لأن الواقف يصح انفراده فكان كالعدم، وظاهر ما في الخانية أنه مفرع على قول أبي يوسف بجواز عزل المتولي بلا شرط، وأما على قول محمد فالواقف كالأجنبي فينبغي أن لا يملك الواقف الاستبدال وحده، وكذا الإدخال والإخراج ولم يظهر لي وجه الثالثة وأما الثانية أعني اشتراط الولاية للواقف فالمذكور قول أبي يوسف وهو قول هلال وهو ظاهر المذهب. وذكر هلال في وقفه وقال أقوام : إن شرط الواقف الولاية لنفسه كانت له وإن لم يشترط لم تكن له ولاية قال مشايخنا. والأشبه أن يكون هذا قول محمد لأن أصله أن التسليم للقيم شرط لصحة الوقف فإذا سلم لم يبق له من ولاية فيه، ولنا أن المتولي إنما يستفيد فيه الولاية من جهته بشرطه فيستحيل أن لا تكون له الولاية وغيره يستفيد الولاية منه ، ولأنه أقرب الناس إلى هذا الوقف فيكون أولى بولايته كمن اتخذ مسجداً يكون أولى بعمارته ونصب المؤذن فيه، وكمن أعتق عبداً كان الولاء له لأنه أقرب الناس إليه ؛ كذا في الهداية وفي الخلاصة : إذا شرط الواقف أن يكون هو المتولي فعند أبي يوسف الوقف والشرط كلاهما صحيحان، وعند محمد وهلال الوقف والشرط كلاهما باطلان اهـ. فقد اختلف النقل عن هلال وفي الخلاصة : إذا شرط في الوقف الولاية لنفسه وأولاده في عزل القيم واستبداله لهم وما هو من نوع الولاية وأخرجه من يد المتولي جاز، ولو لم يشترط الولاية لنفسه وأخرجه من يده قال محمد: لا ولاية للواقف والولاية للقيم، وكذا لو مات وله وصي لا ولاية لوصيه والولاية للقيم. وقال أبو يوسف: الولاية للواقف وله أن يعزل القيم في حياته، وإذا مات الواقف بطل ولاية القيم، ومشايخ بلخ يفتون بقول أبي يوسف وقال الصدر الشهيد والفتوى على قول محمد اهـ. والحاصل أن أبا يوسف لما لم يشترط التسليم إلى المتولي جاز عنده ابتداء شرط التولية إلى نفسه، وإذا ولى غيره كالأولاد مثلاً إذا أسقط حقه يسقط وليس كذلك فإن الشارح له رسالة صرح فيها بعدم الفرق بين فقراء المدرسة وبين الموقوف عليه المعين فتدبر وكذا الشيخ خير الدين في فتواه مشى على عدم الفرق بينهما؛ كذا بخط شيخ شيخنا عبد الحي . ثم رأيت للعلامة الطوري رسالة مشى فيها أن الحق إذا كان لمعين فإنه يسقط بالإسقاط فراجعه يقول الفقير جامع هذه الحواشي : كذا بخط بعض الفضلاء
The Book of Waqf. There occurred fatwa incidents regarding the issue of insertion and removal and so on. Among them: If one who has that right, after having inserted a person, says 'I have dropped my right to remove him,' then removes him, does he [really] remove [him]? And among them: If he says 'I have dropped my right from him,' does it drop and he has no power to do anything? And among them: If the waqf settlor conditions for himself the insertion and removal and so on whenever he wishes, and conditions that he can stipulate it for whomever he wants, then he stipulates it for someone else, and that someone stipulates for him what he stipulated for himself, then the person for whom it was stipulated stipulates it for another, so the one for whom the waqf settlor stipulated it wants to remove the one who made this stipulation, and the one for whom it was made (the beneficiary) wants to remove the maker, so is it for the first or the second? On the basis that when the one for whom it is stipulated makes it for another, does his own right become void or does it remain for him and for the one he made it for? And among them: If he conditions it for himself and for so-and-so, does either of them have the right to act alone or not? I have not seen an explicit transmission regarding them. The apparent [meaning] of what is in al-Khāniyah regarding the drink [right] is that a right is subject to surrender, so he drops his right, for he explicitly stated that the right of the warrior before distribution, the right of the mere watercourse, the right of the legatee of dwelling, the right of the legatee of one-third before distribution, and the right of the heir before distribution drop. And he explicitly stated in Jāmi‘ al-Fuṣūlayn, from the twenty-eighth chapter: If an heir says 'I have left my right,' his right does not become void because ownership is not voided by abandonment, but a right is voided by it, such that if one of the warriors says before distribution 'I have left my right,' his right becomes void, and similarly if the mortgagee says 'I have left my right in detaining the pawn,' it becomes void, end. So his statement 'and the right is voided by it' indicates what we have mentioned. If you say: It is mentioned in al-Khāniyah, from the Book of Testimonies, that whoever is poor among the inhabitants of a school is entitled to the waqf as an entitlement that is not voided by his voiding it, for if he says 'I have voided my right,' he still may demand and take afterwards, end. I say: There is a difference between them because our discussion is where the right is for a specific person and he surrenders it. As for what is in al-Khāniyah from Testimonies, the right is for a non-specific person, for it is an absolute waqf on the poor of the school, and a non-specific person's right cannot be validly voided. And it is only from this principle that the case where the right is not for a specific person is excluded, and similar is in gift. He said in al-Bazzāziyyah: If the donor says 'I have dropped my right to revoke the gift,' it does not drop, end. If you say: If the one who has the condition says 'I have no right nor entitlement nor claim in it,' does he have the authority of insertion and removal along with the settlor's condition? I say: He does not have that because he is admitting that he has no right, and he is held accountable for his admission. That is why al-Khassāf said: If he makes a waqf on his children and then admits that it is upon him and upon Zayd, action is taken upon his admission as long as he lives, on the understanding that the settlor has retracted his specification and included Zayd, etc. And with al-Ramlī, and without this condition, it is not permissible for him to do that. His statement: 'And what is apparent in al-Khāniyah regarding drinking' etc. is used to derive the answer for the first and second. And his statement: 'And what is apparent in Fatḥ al-Qadīr' etc. is used to derive the answer for the fourth. And there remains a pause regarding the third, so he said afterwards: 'And the aspect of the third is not clear to me.' His statement: 'Similarly, if the mortgagee says "I have left my right" etc.' Al-Ramlī said: Later in this commentary, in the chapter on whose testimony is accepted and whose is not, in the explanation of his statement 'the partner to his partner', after some preceding speech, the truth is that whoever drops his right in a function in which it is established that his right drops, then refer to it if you wish. His statement: 'Where the right is for a specific person and he surrenders it' is apparent, rather explicit, that the beneficiary... (Page 377) I was asked about someone who has the right of insertion and removal whenever he wishes; he inserted a person, so what is the legal trick to prevent his removal? I answered: He should declare that he has no right to remove him, and he has no hold on the settlor's condition, so he is not able to remove him afterwards. This is what appeared to me, and Allah knows best. And what is apparent in Fatḥ al-Qadīr is that the issue of the condition of insertion and removal etc. is parallel to the issue of substitution, that the settlor has the sole right and the other does not have sole right, based on what we mentioned from al-Khāniyah regarding the issue when he conditions substitution for himself and for so-and-so, with the reasoning that the settlor is the one who conditioned it for that man, and what he conditioned for another is conditioned for himself, end. And it might be said: Then there is no benefit in conditioning it with him because the settlor's sole action is valid, so it is as if it is non-existent. And what is apparent in al-Khāniyah is that it is derived from the saying of Abū Yūsuf on the permissibility of dismissing the mutawallī without a condition. As for the saying of Muḥammad, the settlor is like a stranger, so it should be that the settlor does not own substitution alone, and likewise insertion and removal. And the aspect of the third is not clear to me. As for the second, meaning the condition of authority for the settlor, the mentioned position is that of Abū Yūsuf, which is also the position of Hilāl, and it is the apparent school. Hilāl mentioned in his waqf, and some people said: If the settlor conditions authority for himself, he has it, and if he does not condition, he does not have authority. Our scholars said: And the more likely is that this is the position of Muḥammad, because his principle is that delivery to the administrator is a condition for the validity of the waqf, so once he delivers, no authority remains for him over it. And for us, the administrator only acquires authority from him by his condition, so it is impossible that he does not have authority while others acquire authority from him, and because he is the closest person to this waqf, so he is more entitled to its authority, like one who builds a mosque is more entitled to its maintenance and appointing the caller to prayer, and like one who emancipates a slave — the patronage belongs to him because he is the closest person to him. Thus in al-Hidāyah. And in al-Khulāṣah: If the settlor conditions that he himself be the administrator, then according to Abū Yūsuf both the waqf and the condition are valid, and according to Muḥammad and Hilāl both are invalid, end. So the transmission from Hilāl differs. And in al-Khulāṣah: If he conditions in the waqf authority for himself and his children in dismissing the administrator and substituting for him and what is of the type of authority, and removes it from the hand of the administrator, it is permissible. And if he does not condition authority for himself and removes it from his hand, Muḥammad said: The settlor has no authority, and authority belongs to the administrator. Similarly, if he dies and has an executor, the executor has no authority, and authority is for the administrator. And Abū Yūsuf said: The authority is for the settlor, and he may dismiss the administrator during his life, and when the settlor dies, the authority of the administrator becomes void. And the scholars of Balkh give fatwa according to Abū Yūsuf's saying, and al-Ṣadr al-Shahīd said: The fatwa is according to Muḥammad's saying, end. And the conclusion: Since Abū Yūsuf did not require delivery to the administrator, according to him, the initial condition of authority for himself is permissible. And when he appoints someone else, like children for example, if he drops his right, it drops. But it is not so, for the commentator has a treatise in which he explicitly stated that there is no difference between the poor of a school and the specific beneficiary, so ponder. Similarly, Shaykh Khayr al-Dīn in his fatwa walked on the absence of difference between them. Thus in the handwriting of the shaykh of our shaykh, ‘Abd al-Ḥayy. Then I saw for al-‘Allāmah al-Ṭūrī a treatise in which he walked on that the right, if it is for a specific person, then it drops by surrender, so refer to it. The poor compiler of these margin notes says: Thus in the handwriting of some virtuous persons.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq is an expansion on the rulings related to conditions of insertion and removal (إدخال وإخراج) in waqf. It first enumerates four specific fatwa incidents that arose concerning such conditions, then provides answers based on the principle that a right (حق) can be surrendered (إسقاط) if it belongs to a specific person (معين), but not if it is for a non-specific group (غير معين). The author distinguishes between the right of a specific beneficiary and the right of the poor of a school, citing al-Khāniyah and Jāmi‘ al-Fuṣūlayn. He then offers a legal trick (حيلة) to prevent removal: the person admitting he has no right. The discussion then shifts to the wāqif's own authority (ولاية) over the waqf, highlighting the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad. Abū Yūsuf holds that the wāqif retains authority even without a condition, while Muḥammad requires delivery to the mutawallī. The author notes that the relied-upon position (muftā bihī) is that of Muḥammad according to al-Ṣadr al-Shahīd, though scholars of Balkh followed Abū Yūsuf. The passage concludes with a note on the difference among later scholars regarding the surrender of rights.

Key Terms
إدخال وإخراج (idkhāl wa ikhrāj): The right to insert new beneficiaries into a waqf or remove existing ones, as conditioned by the wāqif.
حق لمعين (ḥaqq li-mu‘ayyan): A right belonging to a specific named individual, which can be surrendered (isqāt) by that individual.
ولاية الواقف (wilāyat al-wāqif): The authority of the waqf settlor to manage the endowment, appoint or dismiss the mutawallī, etc.
متولي (mutawallī): The administrator appointed by the wāqif to manage the waqf property.
حيلة (hīlah): A legal stratagem or trick to achieve a permissible outcome within the framework of the law. In this passage, it refers to declaring no right to remove.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal trick (حيلة) to prevent a person who has the right of removal from removing someone he has inserted into a waqf?
A) He should explicitly condition that the person cannot be removed.
B) He should declare that he has no right to remove him.
C) He should transfer his right to another person.
D) He should revoke the waqf condition.

Key Takeaway
A specific beneficiary's right in waqf can be surrendered; a non-specific class right cannot. The wāqif's authority after delivery is disputed, with the preferred view being that it ceases.

Hila for Preventing Removal and the Waqif's Authority: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Hila and intra-Hanafi dispute on waqif authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hila for preventing removal of a beneficiary and explain the disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the waqif's stipulation of authority.

Core Idea
The waqif’s authority after delivery is disputed: Abu Yusuf allows stipulation, Muhammad denies it.

This passage presents two interconnected issues in Hanafi waqf law: first, a practical hila for a waqif who wishes to permanently include a beneficiary; second, a foundational intra-madhhab dispute on whether the waqif can retain authority after establishing the waqf. Understanding both requires grasping the underlying principle of delivery (taslim) to the qayyim.

Guided Path
1
Extract the hila for preventing removal
The passage begins with a question: how to prevent the waqif from removing someone he has inserted? Find the answer given: the waqif acknowledges in writing that he has no right to remove.
This is based on giving up the right.
2
Analyze the analogy with istibdal
The author links idkhal wa ikhraj to istibdal. Understand why the waqif's condition for partnership is ineffective: he retains sole authority because he is the source of the condition.
See the quote from al-Khaniyah.
3
State the intra-Hanafi positions on waqif's authority
Abu Yusuf: If waqif stipulates his own authority, both waqf and condition valid. Muhammad: Both invalid. Also, when appointing another: Abu Yusuf says he is an agent; Muhammad says he is not.
These positions stem from differing views on taslim.
4
Evaluate the arguments for each position
Abu Yusuf uses analogy (qiyas) with mosque builder and emancipator. Muhammad relies on the principle that delivery removes the waqif's authority. Compare the strength of each.
Pay attention to the use of qiyas jaliy.
5
Determine the practical consequence and operative fatwa
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Yusuf, the waqif can be mutawalli; under Muhammad he cannot. The fatwa according to al-Sadr al-Shahid is on Muhammad's view, though Balkh scholars followed Abu Yusuf.
This shows how later tarjih operates.

هذا سئلت فيمن له الإدخال والإخراج كلما بدا له فأدخل إنساناً فما الحيلة في عدم جواز إخراجه؟ فأجبت بأنه يقر بأنه لا حق له في إخراجه ولا تمسك له بما في شرط الواقف فلا يقدر على إخراجه بعده هذا ما ظهر لي والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم. وظاهر قوله في فتح القدير أن مسألة شرط الإدخال والإخراج إلى آخره على وزان مسألة الاستبدال أن للواقف الانفراد وليس للآخر الانفراد لما ذكرناه عن الخانية في مسألة ما إذا شرط الاستبدال لنفسه ولفلان معللاً بأن الواقف هو الذي شرط لذلك الرجل وما شرط لغيره فهو مشروط لنفسه اهـ. وقد يقال : لا فائدة حينئذ في اشتراطه معه لأن الواقف يصح انفراده فكان كالعدم، وظاهر ما في الخانية أنه مفرع على قول أبي يوسف بجواز عزل المتولي بلا شرط، وأما على قول محمد فالواقف كالأجنبي فينبغي أن لا يملك الواقف الاستبدال وحده، وكذا الإدخال والإخراج ولم يظهر لي وجه الثالثة وأما الثانية أعني اشتراط الولاية للواقف فالمذكور قول أبي يوسف وهو قول هلال وهو ظاهر المذهب. وذكر هلال في وقفه وقال أقوام : إن شرط الواقف الولاية لنفسه كانت له وإن لم يشترط لم تكن له ولاية قال مشايخنا. والأشبه أن يكون هذا قول محمد لأن أصله أن التسليم للقيم شرط لصحة الوقف فإذا سلم لم يبق له من ولاية فيه، ولنا أن المتولي إنما يستفيد فيه الولاية من جهته بشرطه فيستحيل أن لا تكون له الولاية وغيره يستفيد الولاية منه ، ولأنه أقرب الناس إلى هذا الوقف فيكون أولى بولايته كمن اتخذ مسجداً يكون أولى بعمارته ونصب المؤذن فيه، وكمن أعتق عبداً كان الولاء له لأنه أقرب الناس إليه ؛ كذا في الهداية وفي الخلاصة : إذا شرط الواقف أن يكون هو المتولي فعند أبي يوسف الوقف والشرط كلاهما صحيحان، وعند محمد وهلال الوقف والشرط كلاهما باطلان اهـ. فقد اختلف النقل عن هلال وفي الخلاصة : إذا شرط في الوقف الولاية لنفسه وأولاده في عزل القيم واستبداله لهم وما هو من نوع الولاية وأخرجه من يد المتولي جاز، ولو لم يشترط الولاية لنفسه وأخرجه من يده قال محمد: لا ولاية للواقف والولاية للقيم، وكذا لو مات وله وصي لا ولاية لوصيه والولاية للقيم. وقال أبو يوسف: الولاية للواقف وله أن يعزل القيم في حياته، وإذا مات الواقف بطل ولاية القيم، ومشايخ بلخ يفتون بقول أبي يوسف وقال الصدر الشهيد والفتوى على قول محمد اهـ. والحاصل أن أبا يوسف لما لم يشترط التسليم إلى المتولي جاز عنده ابتداء شرط التولية إلى نفسه، وإذا ولى غيره كالأولاد مثلاً إذا أسقط حقه يسقط وليس كذلك فإن الشارح له رسالة صرح فيها بعدم الفرق بين فقراء المدرسة وبين الموقوف عليه المعين فتدبر وكذا الشيخ خير الدين في فتواه مشى على عدم الفرق بينهما؛ كذا بخط شيخ شيخنا عبد الحي . ثم رأيت للعلامة الطوري رسالة مشى فيها أن الحق إذا كان لمعين فإنه يسقط بالإسقاط فراجعه يقول الفقير جامع هذه الحواشي : كذا بخط بعض الفضلاء 
 قوله : (وإذا ولى غيره كان وكيلاً عنه قال الرملي هذا صريح في أنه يصح عزله بجنحة وغير جنحة عنده لأنه وكيل عنه وللموكل عزل الوكيل مطلقاً وسيذكره قريباً. قوله : (بطلت ولايته إلا إذا جعله قيماً في حياته وبعد مماته كما مر قيل عشرين ورقة. قوله : (ومحمد لما شرطه انعكست الأحكام قال الرملي أي فلا يجوز شرط التولية لنفسه وإذا ولي غيره لا يكون وكيلاً عنه فليس له عزله ولا تبطل ولايته بموته عنده .
This: I was asked about one who has the right to include and exclude whenever he wishes, and he included a person, so what is the legal device to prevent his removal? I answered: He acknowledges that he has no right to remove him and he has no recourse to the condition of the founder, so he will not be able to remove him after that. This is what appeared to me, and Allah knows best. And the apparent meaning of his statement in Fath al-Qadir is that the issue of the condition of inclusion and exclusion is analogous to the issue of substitution: the founder has the sole authority and the other does not have sole authority, as we mentioned from al-Khaniyah regarding the case when he stipulated substitution for himself and for so-and-so, reasoning that the founder is the one who stipulated for that man, and what he stipulated for others is stipulated for himself. It may be said: There is no benefit then in stipulating it with him, because the founder's sole authority is valid, so it is as if it were non-existent. And the apparent meaning of what is in al-Khaniyah is that it is derived from Abu Yusuf's view permitting the removal of the mutawalli without a condition. As for Muhammad's view, the founder is like a stranger, so he should not own the substitution alone, and likewise inclusion and exclusion. And the face of the third has not appeared to me. As for the second, meaning stipulating authority for the founder, what is mentioned is the view of Abu Yusuf and it is the view of Hilal, and it is the apparent madhhab. And Hilal mentioned in his waqf: Some people said: If the founder stipulates authority for himself, he has it; if he does not stipulate, he has no authority. Our scholars said: The most plausible is that this is Muhammad's view, because his principle is that delivery to the qayyim is a condition for the validity of the waqf, so if it is delivered, no authority remains for him in it. And we say: The mutawalli only derives authority from him by his condition, so it is impossible that he should have no authority while another derives authority from him. And because he is the closest person to this waqf, so he is more entitled to its authority, like one who builds a mosque is more entitled to its maintenance and appointing the mu'adhdhin, and like one who emancipates a slave has the wala' because he is the closest. This is in al-Hidayah. And in al-Khulasah: If the founder stipulated that he be the mutawalli, then according to Abu Yusuf both the waqf and condition are valid; according to Muhammad and Hilal both are invalid. So there is a difference in transmission from Hilal. And in al-Khulasah: If he stipulated in the waqf authority for himself and his children in removing the qayyim and replacing him, and what is of the type of authority, and he removed him from the mutawalli's hand, it is permissible. If he did not stipulate authority for himself and removed him from his hand, Muhammad said: There is no authority for the founder, and authority is for the qayyim. Likewise, if he dies and has an executor, the executor has no authority, and authority is for the qayyim. Abu Yusuf said: Authority is for the founder, and he may remove the qayyim during his lifetime, and when the founder dies, the authority of the qayyim is annulled. The scholars of Balkh give fatwa according to Abu Yusuf's view, and al-Sadr al-Shahid said: The fatwa is according to Muhammad's view. The summary: Since Abu Yusuf did not stipulate delivery to the mutawalli, in his view the condition of appointing oneself as mutawalli is initially valid. And if he appoints another, like children, if he drops his right, it is dropped, and it is not so, because the commentator has a treatise in which he clarified that there is no difference between the poor of a school and a specific beneficiary, so reflect. Likewise, Shaykh Khayr al-Din in his fatwa followed the view of no difference between them. This is in the handwriting of the shaykh of our shaykh, 'Abd al-Hayy. Then I saw a treatise by al-'Allamah al-Touri in which he went that the right if it is for a specific person, it drops by dropping it, so consult it. The poor compiler of these notes said: This is in the handwriting of some virtuous person.
His statement: (And if he appoints another, he is his agent) al-Ramli said: This is explicit that it is valid to dismiss him with or without fault according to him, because he is his agent, and the principal may dismiss the agent absolutely, and he will mention it soon. His statement: (His authority is annulled unless he made him a qayyim in his lifetime and after his death, as mentioned twenty pages ago). His statement: (And Muhammad, when he stipulated it, the rulings are reversed) al-Ramli said: i.e., it is not permitted to stipulate authority for himself, and if he appoints another, he is not his agent, so he cannot dismiss him, and his authority is not annulled by his death according to him.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute focusing on the authority of the waqif (founder) regarding the condition of insertion and removal (idkhal wa ikhraj) in waqf. The passage begins with a practical question: what legal device (hila) can be used to prevent a waqif from removing a person he has inserted, if the waqif has the right to insert and remove whenever he wishes? The answer provided is that the waqif should acknowledge in writing that he has no right to remove that person, and he cannot rely on his original condition because he has given up that right. The author then discusses the issue in light of Fath al-Qadir, comparing the shart al-idkhal wa al-ikhraj to the issue of istibdal (substitution). The key point: if the waqif stipulates substitution for himself and another, the waqif alone has the right; the other has none. This is because the waqif is the one who made the condition for the other, but what he did not stipulate for others remains his. Some object: this makes the condition of partnership useless because the waqif alone can act. The author explains that this ruling is based on Abu Yusuf's view that the waqif can dismiss the mutawalli without a condition. Under Muhammad's view, the waqif is like a stranger and cannot exercise sole authority. The passage then delves into the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on whether the waqif can stipulate authority (wilaya) for himself. According to Abu Yusuf, if the waqif stipulates that he himself is the mutawalli, both the waqf and the condition are valid. According to Muhammad and Hilal, both are invalid. The reasoning: Muhammad's principle is that delivery (taslim) to a qayyim is necessary for valid waqf; once delivered, the waqif loses authority. Abu Yusuf argues that the mutawalli's authority derives from the waqif's condition, so the waqif cannot lack what he grants to others. Moreover, the waqif is the closest to the waqf, analogous to the builder of a mosque or the emancipator of a slave. The passage also cites al-Khulasah and the differing transmissions from Hilal. In practice, the scholars of Balkh gave fatwa according to Abu Yusuf, but al-Sadr al-Shahid said the fatwa is according to Muhammad. The marginal notes (by al-Ramli) clarify that when the waqif appoints another as mutawalli, according to Abu Yusuf the appointee is an agent and thus can be dismissed; according to Muhammad, the appointee is not an agent and cannot be dismissed by the waqif, and the appointment does not end with the waqif's death.

Key Terms
الإدخال والإخراج (al-idkhal wa al-ikhraj): The right to include new beneficiaries or remove existing ones from a waqf
الاستبدال (al-istibdal): The right to replace waqf property (usually selling and replacing) with other property
الولاية (al-wilaya): Authority or guardianship over the waqf, including management and appointment decisions

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a waqif stipulates that he himself is the mutawalli?
A) Abu Yusuf says the waqf is valid but the condition is invalid.
B) Muhammad says both the waqf and condition are valid.
C) Abu Yusuf says both the waqf and condition are valid; Muhammad says both are invalid.
D) Both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree that the condition is valid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school internally disputes whether the waqif can retain authority after delivery; the mufta bihi per al-Sadr al-Shahid is Muhammad's view that the condition is invalid.

Conditions for the Nazir (Supervisor) of Waqf
Defines qualifications and conditions for the nazir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the conditions of priority from conditions of validity for the nazir of a waqf, and apply the Hanafi istihsan ruling on the appointment of a minor.

Core Idea
Qualifications for the nazir are mostly priorities—validity requires only puberty and sanity.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies who may serve as the nazir (supervisor) of a waqf. It distinguishes between conditions that are recommended for the ideal candidate and conditions that are legally necessary for a valid appointment. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the Hanafi rules on waqf administration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four topics of discussion
The passage opens by listing four areas regarding the nazir: his qualifications and dismissal, the nazir by condition, the nazir by judge, and his transactions. Locate these in the first sentence.
2
Extract the qualifications listed
From Fath al-Qadir and al-Is'af, list the desirable traits: not seeking office, no known sin, trustworthy, capable, etc. Note that men and women, blind and sighted, and repentant slanderers are treated equally.
3
Categorize as priority vs. validity
The passage explicitly states that most conditions are shurut al-awlawiyyah (conditions of priority) not shurut al-sihhah (conditions of validity). Only puberty and sanity are required for validity.
This distinction is key: violating a priority condition does not invalidate the appointment.
4
Apply istihsan to the minor's appointment
By qiyas, appointing a child is void; but istihsan holds it is suspended until the child matures. Understand this as a relaxation of strict analogy for practical benefit.
5
Understand the removal of a sinful nazir
If the nazir becomes sinful, he deserves removal but is not automatically dismissed. The passive voice 'yukhraj' means he should be removed, analogous to a sinful judge who is not automatically dismissed.
This reinforces that justice ('adala) is a condition of priority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكلام هنا في الناظر يقع في مواضع : الأول في أهله وفيه بيان عزله وعزل أرباب الوظائف الثاني في الناظر بالشرط الثالث في الناظر من القاضي. الرابع في تصرفاته وفيه بيان ما عليه من العمل وماله من الأجرة. أما الأول فقال في فتح القدير : الصالح للنظر من لم يسأل الولاية للوقف وليس فيه فسق يعرف قال : وصرح بأنه مما يخرج به الناظر ما إذا ظهر به فسق کشربه الخمر ونحوه .اهـ. وفي الإسعاف: لا يولى إلا أمين قادر بنفسه أو بنائبه لأن الولاية مقيدة بشرط النظر، وليس من النظر تولية الخائن لأنه يخل بالمقصود، وكذا تولية العاجز لأن المقصود لا يحصل به ويستوي فيه الذكر والأنثى، وكذا الأعمى والبصير، وكذا المحدود في قذف إذا تاب لأنه أمين رجل طلب التولية على الوقف . قالوا: لا يعطى له وهو كمن طلب القضاء لا يقلد .اهـ. والظاهر أنها شرائط الأولوية لا شرائط الصحة وأن الناظر إذا فسق استحق العزل ولا ينعزل لأن القضاء أشرف من التولية ويحتاط فيه أكثر من التولية والعدالة فيه شرط الأولوية حتى يصح تقليد الفاسق، وإذا فسق القاضي لا ينعزل على الصحيح المفتى به فكذا الناظر، ويقرأ يخرج» في عبارة ابن الهمام بالبناء للمجهول أي يجب إخراجه ولا ينعزل. ويشترط للصحة بلوغه وعقله لما في الإسعاف : ولو أوصى إلى صبي تبطل في القياس مطلقاً، وفي الاستحسان هي باطلة ما دام صغيراً، فإذا كبر تكون الولاية له، وحكم من لم يخلق من ولده ونسله في الولاية كحكم الصغير قياساً واستحساناً .اهـ. ولا تشترط الحرية والإسلام للصحة لما في الإسعاف : ولو كان ولده عبداً يجوز قياساً واستحساناً لأهليته في ذاته بدليل أن تصرفه الموقوف لحق المولى ينفذ عليه بعد العتق لزوال المانع بخلاف الصبي والذمي في الحكم كالعبد فلو أخرجهما القاضي 
 في هامش البحر في هذا المحل. ورأيت بعده بخط شيخنا المحشي ما نصه : قلت وقد ذكر المؤلف هذه المسألة في باب من تقبل شهادته ومن لا تقبل عند قوله والشريك لشريكه فراجعه من كتاب الشهادات. 
 قوله : (والظاهر أنها) قال الرملي : أي العدالة في الناظر .اهـ. والظاهر عوده لجميع ما مر بقرينة جمعه الشرائط تأمل . قوله : ( ويشترط للنظر بلوغه الخ) أفتى به العلامة ابن الجلبي فقال في فتاواه وأما الإسناد للصغير فلا يصح بحال لا على سبيل الاستقلال بالنظر ولا على سبيل المشاركة لغيره لأن النظر على الوقف من باب الولاية والصغير يولى
And the discussion here about the nazir falls into topics: First, regarding his qualifications, and in it an explanation of his dismissal and the dismissal of the functionaries. Second, regarding the nazir by condition. Third, regarding the nazir appointed by the judge. Fourth, regarding his transactions, and in it an explanation of what he must do and what he is entitled to as a fee. As for the first, it is said in Fath al-Qadir: The one fit for supervision is one who did not request the authority for the waqf and in whom no known sin exists. He said: And he stated that among things that cause the nazir to be removed is if sin appears in him, such as drinking wine and the like. In al-Is'af: No one is appointed except a trustworthy person, capable himself or through a deputy, because authority is restricted to the condition of supervision, and it is not of supervision to appoint a treacherous person because it harms the objective; likewise appointing an incapable person because the objective is not achieved. In it the male and female are equal, likewise the blind and the sighted, likewise one who has been hadd-punished for slander if he has repented, because he is trustworthy. A man who requests the appointment over a waqf: They said: He should not be given it, and he is like one who requests the judgeship; he is not appointed. The apparent position is that these are conditions of priority, not conditions of validity. If the nazir becomes sinful, he deserves dismissal but is not automatically dismissed, because judgeship is more noble than trusteeship and there is more caution in it than in trusteeship. And justice (adala) in it is a condition of priority, so it is valid to appoint a sinful person. And if the judge becomes sinful, he is not dismissed according to the correct fatwa; similarly the nazir. And the word 'yukhruj' (is removed) in Ibn al-Humam's expression is in the passive voice, meaning he must be removed, but he does not automatically become dismissed. For validity, puberty and sanity are required, as in al-Is'af: If he appoints a child as executor, it is void in qiyas absolutely, and in istihsan it is invalid as long as he is small; when he grows up, the authority becomes his. And the ruling of one who has not yet been created from his offspring and lineage in authority is like the ruling of the minor, by qiyas and istihsan. Freedom and Islam are not conditions for validity, as in al-Is'af: If his child is a slave, it is permissible by qiyas and istihsan because of his inherent eligibility, evidenced by the fact that his suspended transaction for the right of the master becomes effective after emancipation due to the removal of the obstacle, unlike the minor and the dhimmi in ruling like the slave. So if the judge removes both...

And after it I saw in the handwriting of our commentator, may God have mercy on him, the text: I said: The author has mentioned this issue in the chapter on whose testimony is accepted and whose not at his statement 'and the partner of his partner' so consult it from the Book of Testimonies.
His statement: (And the apparent is that it) said al-Ramli: i.e., justice in the nazir. The apparent is its return to all that has passed, by the evidence of his gathering the conditions, reflect. His statement: (And for validity, puberty is required) al-'Allamah Ibn al-Julabi gave a fatwa on it, saying in his fatwas: As for assignment to a minor, it is not valid at all, neither independently nor as a participant with others, because supervision over waqf is a type of authority, and a minor is appointed...
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage defines the qualifications for the nazir (supervisor) of a waqf. It begins by outlining four topics: the qualifications and removal of the nazir and other functionaries, the nazir appointed by condition, the nazir appointed by the judge, and the nazir's transactions. For the first topic, the passage cites Fath al-Qadir: the qualified nazir is one who did not seek the position and in whom no known sin exists; if sin appears (e.g., drinking wine), he should be removed. Al-Is'af adds that only a trustworthy and capable person should be appointed; men and women are equal, as are the blind and sighted; a person who has been hadd-punished for qadhf (slander) is acceptable if he repents. One who requests the position should not be appointed, analogous to one who seeks judgeship. The key point is that these are conditions of priority (shurut al-awlawiyyah) not conditions of validity (shurut al-sihhah). Thus, if the nazir becomes sinful, he deserves dismissal but does not automatically lose office, similar to a judge. The word 'yukhraj' in Ibn al-Humam's expression is passive, meaning he should be removed but is not automatically disqualified. For validity, puberty (bulugh) and sanity ('aql) are required. The passage uses istihsan to allow a child's appointment: it is void while he is a minor but becomes valid when he matures. This applies also to unborn offspring. Freedom and Islam are not conditions for validity: a slave can be appointed, and his transactions are suspended until he is freed; a dhimmi is treated similarly. The marginal notes cross-reference another chapter and clarify that the condition of justice (adala) is a condition of priority, not validity, and that the fatwa of Ibn al-Julabi rejects the appointment of a minor absolutely.

Key Terms
الناظر (al-nazir): The supervisor or administrator of a waqf, responsible for its management
شرائط الأولوية (shurut al-awlawiyyah): Conditions that are recommended but not legally required for validity; their absence does not invalidate the appointment
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that allows a ruling different from qiyas based on considerations of equity or practicality

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition of validity (shart al-sihhah) for the nazir?
A) Trustworthiness (adala)
B) Puberty (bulugh)
C) Freedom (hurriyyah)
D) Not seeking the position

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi waqf law, the nazir's qualifications are primarily conditions of priority; only puberty and sanity are required for a valid appointment.

Conditions of Preference vs. Validity for the Waqf Custodian (Nadhir)
Definition and ruling on waqf overseer qualifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conditions of validity and conditions of preference for the appointment of a nadhir, and apply these distinctions to cases of a fasiq, minor, slave, or dhimmi.

Core Idea
A fasiq can be appointed as waqf overseer – justice is a condition of preference, not validity.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on who qualifies to oversee a waqf. You will see that the school distinguishes sharply between conditions that are essential for the appointment to be valid and conditions that merely make a candidate preferable. This distinction has practical consequences: a sinner (fasiq) may be appointed, though he deserves removal; a minor may be appointed if capable; and a slave or dhimmi may be appointed with certain restrictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nadhir and the discussion framework
The text begins by clarifying that the nadhir (overseer) is appointed by the waqif or judge, and his qualifications are discussed in four sections: qualifications, dismissal, appointment by stipulation, and actions. Focus on the first section.
2
Distinguish conditions of validity from preference
The author states that justice (adala) is a condition of preference, not validity, analogizing to the qadi. Validity requires bulugh (maturity) and aql (sanity). Freedom and Islam are not required.
This distinction is key: preference conditions affect suitability but not the legal status of the appointment.
3
Apply to specific cases
Examine rulings for fasiq (valid but removable), minor (invalid in qiyas, valid in istihsan upon maturity or if capable with adult oversight), slave (permissible with master's permission), and dhimmi (permissible but if removed and later converts, authority does not return automatically).
Each case is derived from sources like al-Isaf and al-Fath al-Qadir.
4
Reconcile apparent contradictions
The passage presents two views on minors: al-Isaf says appointment is invalid until maturity, while al-Ashbah says a capable minor can be appointed with judge placing an adult. The author reconciles by interpreting al-Isaf as referring to a minor without understanding.
This reconciliation is an example of istihsan and ijtihad within the school.

كتاب الوقف

كان وكيلاً عنه فله عزله، وإذا مات الواقف بطلت ولايته ومحمد لما شرطه انعكست الأحكام عنده كما قدمناه والكلام هنا في الناظر يقع في مواضع : الأول في أهله وفيه بيان عزله وعزل أرباب الوظائف الثاني في الناظر بالشرط الثالث في الناظر من القاضي. الرابع في تصرفاته وفيه بيان ما عليه من العمل وماله من الأجرة. أما الأول فقال في فتح القدير : الصالح للنظر من لم يسأل الولاية للوقف وليس فيه فسق يعرف قال : وصرح بأنه مما يخرج به الناظر ما إذا ظهر به فسق کشربه الخمر ونحوه .اهـ. وفي الإسعاف: لا يولى إلا أمين قادر بنفسه أو بنائبه لأن الولاية مقيدة بشرط النظر، وليس من النظر تولية الخائن لأنه يخل بالمقصود، وكذا تولية العاجز لأن المقصود لا يحصل به ويستوي فيه الذكر والأنثى، وكذا الأعمى والبصير، وكذا المحدود في قذف إذا تاب لأنه أمين رجل طلب التولية على الوقف . قالوا: لا يعطى له وهو كمن طلب القضاء لا يقلد .اهـ. والظاهر أنها شرائط الأولوية لا شرائط الصحة وأن الناظر إذا فسق استحق العزل ولا ينعزل لأن القضاء أشرف من التولية ويحتاط فيه أكثر من التولية والعدالة فيه شرط الأولوية حتى يصح تقليد الفاسق، وإذا فسق القاضي لا ينعزل على الصحيح المفتى به فكذا الناظر، ويقرأ يخرج» في عبارة ابن الهمام بالبناء للمجهول أي يجب إخراجه ولا ينعزل. ويشترط للصحة بلوغه وعقله لما في الإسعاف : ولو أوصى إلى صبي تبطل في القياس مطلقاً، وفي الاستحسان هي باطلة ما دام صغيراً، فإذا كبر تكون الولاية له، وحكم من لم يخلق من ولده ونسله في الولاية كحكم الصغير قياساً واستحساناً .اهـ. ولا تشترط الحرية والإسلام للصحة لما في الإسعاف : ولو كان ولده عبداً يجوز قياساً واستحساناً لأهليته في ذات بدليل أن تصرفه الموقوف لحق المولى ينفذ عليه بعد العتق لزوال المانع بخلاف الصبي والذمي في الحكم كالعبد فلو أخرجهما القاضي ثم أعتق العبد وأسلم الذمي لا تعود الولاية إليهما .اهـ.
In the margin of al-Bahr at this place. And I saw after it in the handwriting of our teacher the commentator what follows: I said: The author has mentioned this issue in the chapter on whose testimony is accepted and whose is not, at his statement 'and the partner for his partner', so refer to it from the Book of Testimonies. His statement: (If he appoints someone else, he is his agent) al-Ramli said: This is explicit that it is valid to dismiss him with or without fault according to him, because he is his agent, and the principal has the right to dismiss the agent absolutely, and it will be mentioned soon. His statement: (His authority becomes void) unless he made him executor during his life and after his death as has passed about twenty pages earlier. His statement: (According to Muhammad, since he stipulated them, the rulings are reversed) al-Ramli said: That is, it is not permissible to stipulate the appointment for himself, and if he appoints someone else, he is not his agent, so he does not have the right to dismiss him, nor does his authority become void at his death according to him. His statement: (And it seems that they are) al-Ramli said: That is, 'justice' in the overseer. End. The apparent meaning is that it applies to all that has passed based on the context of the conditions, so reflect. His statement: (And for the appointment it is required that he be an adult, etc.) The scholar Ibn al-Jalabi gave a fatwa on this and said in his Fatawa: As for assigning to a minor, it is not valid at all, neither independently nor by partnership with another, because overseeing the waqf is a type of authority, and the minor is under authority due to his deficiency, so he cannot be put in authority over others. End. But it is stated in al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair in the rulings on children: He is suitable as a wasi and overseer, and the judge appoints an adult in his place until he reaches maturity, as in the versified work of Ibn Wahban on bequests. End. I say: I saw in Ahkam al-Sighar by Imam al-Ustrufshani what follows: In Fatawa Rashid al-Din, may Allah have mercy on him: The judge may delegate the appointment to a minor if he is capable of preservation, and he has the authority to act, just as the judge may permit the minor even if the guardian does not permit, and similarly the appointment. And appointment of a slave who is not restricted is permissible because the obstacle is the right of the master, and that has been removed by permission. End. From this reconciliation is taken, by interpreting what is in al-Isaf as when he is not capable of preservation, i.e., he is a minor without understanding, and what is in al-Ashbah as when he is capable, so consider.

Book of Waqf

He was the agent for him, so he has the right to dismiss him, and when the waqif dies his authority becomes void, and according to Muhammad, since he stipulated them, the rulings are reversed as we have mentioned. And the discussion here regarding the overseer occurs in several places: First, regarding his qualifications, which includes the explanation of his dismissal and the dismissal of those in positions; second, regarding the overseer by stipulation; third, regarding the overseer appointed by the judge; fourth, regarding his actions, which includes an explanation of what he must do and the compensation he is entitled to. As for the first, it is stated in Fath al-Qadir: The one qualified for oversight is one who did not request the position of the waqf and does not have known transgression. He said: And it is explicitly stated that what removes the overseer is when transgression appears, such as drinking alcohol and the like. End. In al-Isaf: Only a trustworthy person capable personally or through his deputy is appointed, because the authority is restricted by the condition of oversight, and appointing a traitor is not part of oversight because it undermines the objective. Likewise, appointing an incapable person because the objective is not achieved. Equality applies between male and female, and between blind and sighted, and one who has been subject to hadd for slander if he has repented, because he is trustworthy. A man who seeks appointment over the waqf: They said: He is not given it, just like one who seeks judgeship is not appointed. End. And it seems that these are conditions of preference, not conditions of validity, and that if the overseer becomes sinful, he deserves dismissal but is not automatically dismissed, because judgeship is more noble than appointment and is more precautionary. Justice is a condition of preference so that appointing a sinful person is valid; and if a judge becomes sinful, he is not automatically dismissed according to the correct and fatwa-worthy view, and similarly the overseer. The word 'yukhraj' in Ibn al-Humam's phrase is read in the passive voice, i.e., he must be removed, but he is not automatically dismissed. For validity, reaching maturity and sanity are required, according to al-Isaf: If one bequeaths to a minor, it is absolutely invalid in qiyas, and in istihsan it is invalid while he is minor; when he grows up, the authority becomes his. The ruling of one who is not created from his children and offspring in terms of authority is like the ruling of a minor in qiyas and istihsan. End. Freedom and Islam are not required for validity according to al-Isaf: If his child is a slave, it is permissible in qiyas and istihsan because of his inherent capability, as evidenced by the fact that his transaction contingent on the master's right is executed after manumission due to the removal of the obstacle, unlike the minor and the dhimmi who are like the slave in ruling. If the judge removes them, then the slave becomes free and the dhimmi converts to Islam, the authority does not return to them. End.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling on the qualifications (ahl) of the nadhir (overseer/custodian) of a waqf. The author begins by stating that the nadhir must not have asked for the post and must not be known for transgression. However, these are conditions of preference (shurut al-awlawiyya), not conditions of validity (shurut al-sihha). Thus, if a fasiq (sinner) is appointed, the appointment is valid, but he deserves to be removed. This is analogous to the qadi: a fasiq qadi is appointed validly but should be removed. The passage then discusses the validity of appointing minors, slaves, and dhimmis. According to al-Isaf, bequeathing authority to a minor is invalid in qiyas but valid in istihsan once the minor reaches maturity. However, other sources like al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair allow a minor to be appointed as overseer if he is capable, with the judge placing an adult to act until the minor matures. The author reconciles these views by interpreting al-Isaf as referring to a minor without understanding. For slaves, appointment is permissible because the master's right can be removed by permission. For dhimmis, appointment is also permissible, but if the judge removes them and later they become free or convert, authority does not automatically return.

Key Terms
الناظر (al-nadhir): The overseer or custodian appointed to manage a waqf.
الفسق (al-fisq): Open sin or transgression, which disqualifies a nadhir from preference but not validity.
شرائط الأولوية (shurut al-awlawiyya): Conditions that make a candidate preferable, not essential for validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, what is the ruling if a fasiq (sinner) is appointed as a nadhir?
A) The appointment is invalid from the start.
B) The appointment is valid but he should be removed.
C) The appointment is valid and he cannot be removed.
D) The appointment is voidable at the option of the beneficiaries.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi waqf law, justice is a condition of preference for the nadhir, not validity, so a fasiq appointment is valid but removable.

Waqf — Endowment

Dismissal of the Nadhir and Qadi's Authority in Waqf
Explains dismissal rules and qadi's waqf authority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for dismissing a nadhir and apply the condition that the qadi's actions require a clear maslaha.

Core Idea
A qadi cannot dismiss a nadhir without cause or create new waqf positions without the waqif's stipulation.

This passage addresses two key questions: Who can dismiss a waqf administrator (nadhir), and when? And what powers does the qadi have over waqf? The Hanafi school presents a nuanced view: the waqif may have broad dismissal power (according to Abu Yusuf), while the qadi is tightly bound—he can only dismiss for wrongdoing and cannot appoint officials unless there is a manifest public benefit. Understanding these limits preserves the waqif's conditions and prevents abuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two dismissal scenarios
The passage distinguishes dismissal by the waqif from dismissal by the qadi. Note that they have different rules.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on waqif's dismissal
Abu Yusuf treats the nadhir as the waqif's agent, so the waqif may dismiss without cause. Muhammad disagrees, viewing the waqf as a binding trust. Identify each position and its basis.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the condition for qadi's dismissal
The qadi can only dismiss a nadhir if there is a wrongdoing (jinhah). This is a stricter requirement than for the waqif.
Jinhah is any transgression; the qadi cannot act arbitrarily.
4
Understand the qadi's limited authority over waqf appointments
The qadi may only deviate from the waqif's stipulations if there is a clear maslaha. The example of appointing a farash shows that even a seeming benefit does not justify creating a vested right without the waqif's condition.
The qadi can hire a servant for wages, but not create a permanent position.
5
Apply the rule to the farash example
If the waqif did not stipulate a janitor, the qadi cannot appoint one as a right. Instead, the administrator can hire a janitor for wages. This preserves the waqif's condition while serving the mosque.
This illustrates the principle that the qadi's actions are restricted by the waqif's conditions.

Source Text

وأما عزله فقدمنا أن أبا يوسف جوز عزله للواقف بغير جنحة وشرط لأنه وكيله وخالفه محمد وأما عزل القاضي له فشرطه أن يكون بجنحة. قال في الإسعاف ولو جعلها للموقوف عليه ولم يكن أهلاً أخرجه القاضي وإن كانت الغلة له وولي عليه مأموناً لأن مرجع الوقف للمساكين وغير المأمون لا يؤمن عليه من تخريب أو بيع فيمتنع وصوله إليهم، ولو أوصى الواقف إلى جماعة وكان بعضهم غير مأمون بدله القاضي بمأمون ، وإن رأى إقامة واحد منهم مقامه فلا بأس به اهـ. وفي جامع الفصولين من الثالث عشر : القاضي لا يملك نصب وصي وقيم مع بقاء وصي الميت وقيمه إلا عند ظهور الخيانة منهما. ومن الفصل الأول معزياً إلى فوائد شيخ الإسلام برهان الدين: شرط الواقف أن يكون المتولي من أولاده وأولاد أولاده هل للقاضي أن يولي غيره بلا خيانة؟ ولو ولاه هل يصير متولياً؟ قال : لا اهـ. فقد أفاد حرمة تولية غيره وعدم صحتها لو فعل. وفي القنية : نصب القاضي قيماً آخر لا ينعزل الأول إن كان منصوب الواقف اهـ. والحاصل أن تصرف القاضي في الأوقاف مقيد بالمصلحة لا أنه يتصرف كيف شاء، فلو فعل ما يخالف شرط الواقف فإنه لا يصح إلا لمصلحة ظاهرة ولذا قال في الذخيرة وغيرها : القاضي إذا قرر فراشاً في المسجد بغير شرط الواقف وجعل له معلوماً فإنه لا يحل للقاضي ذلك ولا يحل للفراش تناول المعلوم اهـ . فإن قلت : في تقرير الفراش مصلحة قلت: يمكن خدمة المسجد بدون تقريره بأن يستأجر المتولي فراشاً له والممنوع تقريره في وظيفة تكون حقاً له ولذا صرح قاضيخان بأن للمتولي أن يستأجر خادماً للمسجد بأجرة المثل، واستفيد منه عدم صحة تقرير القاضي في بقية الوظائف بغير شرط الواقف كشهادة ومباشرة وطلب بالأولى وحرمة المرتبات.

في هامش البحر في هذا المحل. ورأيت بعده بخط شيخنا المحشي ما نصه: قلت وقد ذكر المؤلف هذه المسألة في باب من تقبل شهادته ومن لا تقبل عند قوله والشريك لشريكه فراجعه من كتاب الشهادات. قوله : (وإذا ولى غيره كان وكيلاً عنه قال الرملي هذا صريح في أنه يصح عزله بجنحة وغير جنحة عنده لأنه وكيل عنه وللموكل عزل الوكيل مطلقاً وسيذكره قريباً. قوله : (بطلت ولايته إلا إذا جعله قيماً في حياته وبعد مماته كما مر قيل عشرين ورقة. قوله : (ومحمد لما شرطه انعكست الأحكام قال الرملي أي فلا يجوز شرط التولية لنفسه وإذا ولي غيره لا يكون وكيلاً عنه فليس له عزله ولا تبطل ولايته بموته عنده . قوله : (والظاهر أنها) قال الرملي : أي العدالة في الناظر .اهـ. والظاهر عوده لجميع ما مر بقرينة جمعه الشرائط تأمل . قوله : ( ويشترط للنظر بلوغه الخ) أفتى به العلامة ابن الجلبي فقال في فتاواه وأما الإسناد للصغير فلا يصح بحال لا على سبيل الاستقلال بالنظر ولا على سبيل المشاركة لغيره لأن النظر على الوقف من باب الولاية والصغير يولى عليه لقصوره فلا أن يولى على غيره .اهـ لكن قال في الأشباه والنظائر في أحكام الصبيان : ويصلح وصياً وناظراً ويقيم القاضي مكانه بالغاً إلى بلوغه كما في منظومة ابن وهبان من الوصايا اهـ. أقول : ورأيت في أحكام الصغار للإمام الأستروشني ما نصه : وفي فتاوی رشید الدین رحمه الله : القاضي إذا فوض التولية إلى صبي يجوز إذا كان أهلاً للحفظ ويكون له ولاية التصرف كما أن القاضي يملك إذن الصبي وإن كان الولي لا يأذن وكذلك التولية، وتجوز التولية إلى العبد الغير المحجور عليه لأن المانع حق المولى وقد زال ذلك بالإذن .اهـ. ويؤخذ منه التوفيق بحمل ما في الإسعاف على ما إذا لم يكن أهلاً للحفظ بأن كان صغيراً لا يعقل وما في الأشباه على ما إذا كان أهلاً فتدبر .

وأما عزله فقدمنا أن أبا يوسف جوز عزله للواقف بغير جنحة وشرط لأنه وكيله وخالفه محمد وأما عزل القاضي له فشرطه أن يكون بجنحة. قال في الإسعاف ولو جعلها للموقوف عليه ولم يكن أهلاً أخرجه القاضي وإن كانت الغلة له وولي عليه مأموناً لأن مرجع الوقف للمساكين وغير المأمون لا يؤمن عليه من تخريب أو بيع فيمتنع وصوله إليهم، ولو أوصى الواقف إلى جماعة وكان بعضهم غير مأمون بدله القاضي بمأمون ، وإن رأى إقامة واحد منهم مقامه فلا بأس به اهـ. وفي جامع الفصولين من الثالث عشر : القاضي لا يملك نصب وصي وقيم مع بقاء وصي الميت وقيمه إلا عند ظهور الخيانة منهما. ومن الفصل الأول معزياً إلى فوائد شيخ الإسلام برهان الدين: شرط الواقف أن يكون المتولي من أولاده وأولاد أولاده هل للقاضي أن يولي غيره بلا خيانة؟ ولو ولاه هل يصير متولياً؟ قال : لا اهـ. فقد أفاد حرمة تولية غيره وعدم صحتها لو فعل. وفي القنية : نصب القاضي قيماً آخر لا ينعزل الأول إن كان منصوب الواقف اهـ. والحاصل أن تصرف القاضي في الأوقاف مقيد بالمصلحة لا أنه يتصرف كيف شاء، فلو فعل ما يخالف شرط الواقف فإنه لا يصح إلا لمصلحة ظاهرة ولذا قال في الذخيرة وغيرها : القاضي إذا قرر فراشاً في المسجد بغير شرط الواقف وجعل له معلوماً فإنه لا يحل للقاضي ذلك ولا يحل للفراش تناول المعلوم اهـ . فإن قلت : في تقرير الفراش مصلحة قلت: يمكن خدمة المسجد بدون تقريره بأن يستأجر المتولي فراشاً له والممنوع تقريره في وظيفة تكون حقاً له ولذا صرح قاضيخان بأن للمتولي أن يستأجر خادماً للمسجد بأجرة المثل، واستفيد منه عدم صحة تقرير القاضي في بقية الوظائف بغير شرط الواقف كشهادة ومباشرة وطلب بالأولى وحرمة المرتبات
As for his dismissal, we have already mentioned that Abu Yusuf permitted the waqif to dismiss him without fault or condition because he is his agent, and Muhammad disagreed with him. As for the judge's dismissal of him, its condition is that there be a wrongdoing. It is stated in al-Isaf: If he made the waqf for the beneficiary and he is not qualified, the judge removes him, even if the proceeds are for him, and he appoints a trustworthy person over him, because the ultimate destination of the waqf is to the poor, and one who is not trustworthy is not safe from damage or sale, preventing its reaching them. If the waqif bequeathed to a group and some of them are not trustworthy, the judge replaces them with trustworthy ones; and if he sees fit to appoint one of them in his place, there is no harm. End. In Jami' al-Fusulayn from the thirteenth section: The judge does not have the power to appoint a wasi or executor while the deceased's wasi and executor remain, except when betrayal appears from them. From the first section, attributed to the benefits of Shaykh al-Islam Burhan al-Din: If the waqif stipulated that the administrator be from his children and their children, does the judge have the authority to appoint someone else without betrayal? And if he appoints him, does he become administrator? He said: No. End. So it conveys the prohibition of appointing someone else and its invalidity if done. In al-Quniyah: If the judge appoints another executor, the first is not dismissed if he was appointed by the waqif. End. The upshot is that the judge's actions regarding awqaf are restricted by the public interest; he does not act as he pleases. Thus, if he does something that violates the waqif's stipulation, it is not valid unless there is a clear benefit. For this reason it is stated in al-Dhakhirah and others: If the judge appoints a janitor (farash) in the mosque without the waqif's stipulation and fixes a salary for him, that is not permissible for the judge, and it is not permissible for the janitor to take the salary. End. If you say: In appointing a janitor there is benefit, I say: The mosque can served without such appointment by the administrator hiring a janitor for equivalent wages. What is prohibited is appointing him to a position that becomes a right for him. For this reason Qadikhan stated that the administrator may hire a servant for the mosque at the equivalent wage. From this it is inferred that the judge's appointment is not valid for other positions without the waqif's stipulation, such as testimony, directorship, and request, and the unlawfulness of fixed salaries.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the dismissal of the nadhir and the scope of the qadi's authority over waqf. The author first presents the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that the waqif can dismiss his appointee without cause, treating the nadhir as the waqif's agent; Muhammad disagrees and considers the waqif bound by his stipulations. For the qadi, dismissal requires wrongdoing (jinhah). The passage then cites al-Isaf and other works to illustrate when the qadi may replace an unqualified beneficiary or trustee. A key principle is that the qadi's actions must serve a clear public interest (maslaha) and cannot violate the waqif's conditions unless there is a manifest benefit. The example of appointing a janitor (farash) for a mosque without the waqif's stipulation is given: such an appointment is invalid, and the qadi cannot set a salary. The commentator argues that the mosque can be maintained by the administrator hiring a servant with equivalent wages, so there is no need for a formal appointment. This establishes that the qadi cannot create new endowed positions without the waqif's condition, and any fixed salaries (muratabāt) from such appointments are unlawful.

Key Terms
الجنحة (al-jinhah): Wrongful act or transgression; required for the qadi to dismiss a nadhir.
المصلحة الظاهرة (al-maslaha al-zāhira): A manifest public interest that justifies the qadi deviating from the waqif's stipulations.
الفراش (al-farrāsh): A janitor or attendant in the mosque; the example used to illustrate the qadi's limited authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition must exist for the qadi to dismiss a nadhir?
A) The nadhir must be guilty of a wrongdoing (jinhah).
B) The waqif must request it.
C) A majority of beneficiaries must agree.
D) The qadi can dismiss at any time.

Key Takeaway
The qadi's authority over waqf is strictly limited: he can only dismiss a nadhir for wrongdoing and cannot deviate from the waqif's conditions unless there is a clear public interest.

Removal of the Mutawalli: Waqif vs Qadi
Intra-Hanafi dispute on removal conditions for mutawalli

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad on removal of the mutawalli and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
The waqif can remove the mutawalli without fault per Abu Yusuf, but Imam Muhammad disagrees; the qadi always requires fault.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi disagreement on who can remove the mutawalli (trustee) of a waqf and under what conditions. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents the views of Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, and then clarifies the qadi's role. Understanding this dispute helps you navigate the rights of the waqif and the protection of the waqf's beneficiaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their positions
Abu Yusuf holds that the waqif can remove the mutawalli without any fault or condition. Imam Muhammad disagrees, requiring a cause. The qadi can only remove if there is fault (jinahah).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; both are from the same school.
2
Trace the basis for Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf argues the mutawalli is the waqif's agent (wakil), so the principal can dismiss the agent at will. This is a straightforward application of agency law.
The mutawalli is not a guardian of the beneficiaries; he is the waqif's representative.
3
Understand Muhammad's objection
Imam Muhammad likely sees the mutawalli's appointment as a right of the beneficiaries, not revocable arbitrarily. The passage does not detail his proof, but the disagreement is recorded.
Muhammad's view aligns with a stricter protection of the waqf's continuity.
4
Note the qadi's removal rule and its application
Both agree the qadi removes only if there is fault. If the mutawalli is the beneficiary and is unqualified, the qadi removes him and appoints a trustworthy person. Similarly, if a group of mutawallis includes an untrustworthy member, the qadi substitutes them.
The qadi's power is supervisory, not arbitrary.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the mufta bihi (Abu Yusuf), a waqif can remove a mutawalli at any time without cause. Under Muhammad, the waqif cannot. This difference affects the waqif's control and the mutawalli's security of tenure.
The relied-upon position in fatwa is Abu Yusuf's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما عزله فقدمنا أن أبا يوسف جوز عزله للواقف بغير جنحة وشرط لأنه وكيله وخالفه محمد وأما عزل القاضي له فشرطه أن يكون بجنحة. قال في الإسعاف ولو جعلها للموقوف عليه ولم يكن أهلاً أخرجه القاضي وإن كانت الغلة له وولي عليه مأموناً لأن مرجع الوقف للمساكين وغير المأمون لا يؤمن عليه من تخريب أو بيع فيمتنع وصوله إليهم، ولو أوصى الواقف إلى جماعة وكان بعضهم غير مأمون بدله القاضي بمأمون ، وإن رأى إقامة واحد منهم مقامه فلا بأس به اهـ.
As for his removal, we have already mentioned that Abu Yusuf permitted the waqif to remove him without fault or condition because he is his agent, while Muhammad disagreed with him. As for the qadi's removal of him, its condition is that there be fault. In al-Iscaf: If he made it for the beneficiary and he was not qualified, the qadi removes him, even if the yield is for him, and appoints a trustworthy person over him, because the reference of the waqf is to the needy, and the untrustworthy cannot be trusted not to damage or sell, so its reaching them is prevented. If the waqif appointed a group and some were untrustworthy, the qadi replaces them with trustworthy ones, and if he sees fit to appoint one of them in their place, there is no harm in that.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the removal of the mutawalli (trustee) in a waqf. It opens by stating that the waqif, according to Abu Yusuf, may remove the mutawalli without any fault or stipulated condition, because the mutawalli is his agent (wakil). Imam Muhammad disagrees; he does not permit removal without cause. As for removal by the qadi, both agree it requires a fault (jinahah) on the mutawalli's part. The passage then quotes al-Iscaf, ruling that if the waqif made the beneficiary himself the mutawalli but the beneficiary is not qualified (e.g., a minor or incompetent), the qadi removes him and appoints a trustworthy trustee, even though the yield is for that beneficiary. The reason is that the waqf ultimately benefits the poor, and an untrustworthy person may waste or sell the property. Similarly, if the waqif appointed a group and some are untrustworthy, the qadi replaces them with trustworthy ones. If the qadi chooses to retain one as sufficient, that is permitted.

Key Terms
الواقف (al-wāqif): The person who establishes the endowment (waqf).
المتولي (al-mutawallī): The trustee or manager of the waqf property, appointed by the waqif or by the qadi.
الجنحة (al-jināḥah): Fault or misconduct on the part of the mutawalli that justifies removal by the qadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, why can the waqif remove the mutawalli without fault or condition?
A) Because the mutawalli is an employee of the waqf
B) Because the mutawalli is an agent (wakil) of the waqif
C) Because the mutawalli is the guardian of the beneficiaries
D) Because the waqif retains ownership of the waqf property

Key Takeaway
The waqif's removal of the mutawalli without fault is valid per the mufta bihi (Abu Yusuf); the qadi's removal always requires fault.

Limits of Qadi's Power over Waqf Trustees
Rulings restricting qadi from replacing trustees without cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a qadi may override a waqif's stipulation for trustee appointment and explain the Hanafi restriction of qadi's authority to manifest maslaha.

Core Idea
The qadi cannot replace a waqif-appointed trustee without betrayal or manifest maslaha.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq compiles several rulings that define the boundaries of a qadi's authority over waqf trustees. It emphasizes that the qadi is bound by the waqif's conditions and cannot arbitrarily appoint or remove trustees. The key principle is that any deviation from the waqif's stipulations requires a manifest benefit (maslaha zahirah), and even then, alternative arrangements may make such appointments unnecessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
The qadi cannot appoint a new trustee while the original trustee appointed by the deceased or waqif exists, unless betrayal appears. This is stated in Jami' al-Fusulain.
This applies to wasi, qayyim, and mutawalli.
2
Recognize the scope of the ruling
The ruling covers not only executors but also any trustee appointed by the waqif. The qadi's appointment of another person does not remove the original trustee appointed by the waqif (from al-Qunya).
The waqif's condition is paramount.
3
Understand the exception
The qadi may only deviate from the waqif's condition for a manifest maslaha (clear benefit). Even then, if the existing trustee can achieve the same benefit (e.g., by hiring a servant), the qadi's appointment is invalid.
The manifest maslaha must be genuine and cannot be achieved otherwise.
4
Apply the example of the farash
If the qadi appoints a farash (mosque servant) without the waqif's condition, it is prohibited because the mutawalli can hire one at market rate. This shows that the existence of an alternative negates the claim of manifest maslaha.
Analogous to all religious positions (shahadah, directorship, etc.)
5
Deduce the general rule
By priority (bi al-awla), the prohibition extends to all appointments contrary to waqif's conditions. The qadi's power is restricted, not absolute.
Conclusion: qadi's actions are bound by waqif's stipulations unless manifest maslaha and no alternative.

جماعة وكان بعضهم غير مأمون بدله القاضي بمأمون ، وإن رأى إقامة واحد منهم مقامه فلا بأس به اهـ. وفي جامع الفصولين من الثالث عشر : القاضي لا يملك نصب وصي وقيم مع بقاء وصي الميت وقيمه إلا عند ظهور الخيانة منهما. ومن الفصل الأول معزياً إلى فوائد شيخ الإسلام برهان الدين: شرط الواقف أن يكون المتولي من أولاده وأولاد أولاده هل للقاضي أن يولي غيره بلا خيانة؟ ولو ولاه هل يصير متولياً؟ قال : لا اهـ. فقد أفاد حرمة تولية غيره وعدم صحتها لو فعل. وفي القنية : نصب القاضي قيماً آخر لا ينعزل الأول إن كان منصوب الواقف اهـ. والحاصل أن تصرف القاضي في الأوقاف مقيد بالمصلحة لا أنه يتصرف كيف شاء، فلو فعل ما يخالف شرط الواقف فإنه لا يصح إلا لمصلحة ظاهرة ولذا قال في الذخيرة وغيرها : القاضي إذا قرر فراشاً في المسجد بغير شرط الواقف وجعل له معلوماً فإنه لا يحل للقاضي ذلك ولا يحل للفراش تناول المعلوم اهـ . فإن قلت : في تقرير الفراش مصلحة قلت: يمكن خدمة المسجد بدون تقريره بأن يستأجر المتولي فراشاً له والممنوع تقريره في وظيفة تكون حقاً له ولذا صرح قاضيخان بأن للمتولي أن يستأجر خادماً للمسجد بأجرة المثل، واستفيد منه عدم صحة تقرير القاضي في بقية الوظائف بغير شرط الواقف كشهادة ومباشرة وطلب بالأولى وحرمة المرتبات
And in Jami' al-Fusulain, from the thirteenth: The qadi does not have the authority to appoint a wasi or qayyim while the deceased's wasi and qayyim remain, except when betrayal appears from them. And from the first chapter, citing Fawaid Shaykh al-Islam Burhan al-Din: If the waqif stipulates that the mutawalli be from his children or grandchildren, can the qadi appoint someone else without betrayal? And if he does appoint, does he become mutawalli? He said: No. So it conveys the prohibition of appointing another and its invalidity if done. And in al-Qunya: The qadi's appointment of another qayyim does not remove the first if he was appointed by the waqif. The conclusion is that the qadi's actions regarding waqfs are restricted to maslaha (benefit), not that he acts as he wishes. If he does something contrary to the waqif's condition, it is invalid unless for a manifest maslaha. Hence it is said in al-Dhakhirah and others: If the qadi appoints a farash (servant) in the mosque without the waqif's condition and assigns him a salary, that is not permissible for the qadi, nor is it permissible for the farash to accept the salary. If you say: In appointing a farash there is maslaha, I say: The service of the mosque can be done without appointing him, by the mutawalli hiring a farash for it. What is prohibited is his appointment to a position that becomes a right for him. Hence Qadikhan explicitly stated that the mutawalli may hire a servant for the mosque at the market rate. From this it is deduced the invalidity of the qadi's appointment for other positions without the waqif's condition, such as shahadah (witness position), directorship, and by priority, higher positions, and the prohibition of salaries.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq compiles several rulings that restrict the qadi's power over waqf appointments. The point of departure is Jami' al-Fusulain: the qadi cannot appoint a new wasi or qayyim while the one appointed by the deceased still exists, unless betrayal appears. The same applies to the waqif's stipulation for his descendants: the qadi cannot appoint an outsider without betrayal, and such appointment is invalid. Al-Qunya adds that if the qadi appoints another, it does not remove the original trustee appointed by the waqif. The general principle is that the qadi is bound by the waqif's stipulations and can only act for a manifest maslaha. The example of a mosque farash illustrates: if the qadi appoints a servant not stipulated by the waqif, it is prohibited, because the mutawalli can hire one at market rate. This prohibition applies by analogy to all religious positions (like witness, director). The passage also reiterates the earlier ruling about removal: Abu Yusuf permits the waqif to remove without fault; Muhammad disagrees. The lay student should note that the qadi's power is not arbitrary; it is checked by the waqif's conditions and the requirement of manifest benefit.

Key Terms
الوصي (al-waṣī): An executor or guardian appointed by a deceased person to manage his estate or minor children.
القيم (al-qayyim): A caretaker or trustee, often used interchangeably with mutawalli in waqf context.
المصلحة الظاهرة (al-maṣlaḥah al-ẓāhirah): A manifest benefit that justifies overriding the waqif's condition in waqf management.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the general rule regarding the qadi's power to appoint a trustee for a waqf?
A) The qadi has full discretion to appoint any trustee he sees fit.
B) The qadi is bound by the waqif's conditions and can only appoint a different trustee if the existing one betrays or there is a manifest benefit.
C) The qadi can always appoint a new trustee if he deems it beneficial.
D) The qadi can never appoint a new trustee even with the waqif's permission.

Key Takeaway
The qadi's authority over waqf trustees is strictly limited: he cannot replace a waqif-appointed trustee without betrayal or manifest maslaha, and even then, appointments against conditions are invalid.
