Book of Waqf: A mosque designated for recitation, he does not thereafter have the right to give it to another from outside the people of that locality for recitation. This indicates the specification of the locality and its people. If you say: What the holder of the position takes—is it a wage, charity, or gift? I say: Al-Tarsusi said in Anfa' al-Wasa'il: It contains an admixture of wage, gift, and charity. We considered the element of wage regarding the time of direct service and the corresponding portion of the stipend, and we considered the element of gift with regard to the teacher if he receives his stipend and then dies or is removed, in that he does not have to return the portion for the remainder of the year, and we applied the element of charity to validate the original endowment, for an endowment is not valid for the rich initially because it requires a starting point of a village and cannot exist without observing the aspect of charity. Then he said before that: What is taken is in the sense of a wage, otherwise it would not be permissible for a rich person. So if the teacher dies during the year before the crop comes and before it appears from the land, and he has worked for a period, then dies or is removed, one should look at the time of distributing the crop to the duration of his service and to the service of the one after him, and spread the stipend over the teachers, and see how much is for the separated and the connected teacher, and give him proportionally to his duration, and not consider in his case what we mentioned about considering the time of the crop coming and its realization, as was considered for the children in the endowment upon them. Rather, the ruling differs between them and the teacher, the jurist, and the holder of any position in charitable areas, and this is more appropriate to fiqh and more just, etc. This incident occurred frequently in Cairo, and some Hanafis gave fatwa according to what was said for children, considering the time of the crop's arrival, to the extent that some of them vacate their position before the crop arrives by a month or a week, when they had served most of the year, and the one appointed after him disputes with him, relying on what we mentioned, but this is not correct because of what you know from Tarsusi's statement about dividing the stipend between them according to service. But in Cairo, installments are considered, for they lease the endowments for a rent that is due on the crop, the mere recitation as mentioned. And with this, you know the ruling of what is customary in our time of taking payment for dhikr and recitation in the tahalil and khatmah, regardless of whether it is in the orphans' house and from their wealth when there is no will. There is no power and no strength except through Allah, the Exalted, the Great. Al-Ramli mentioned that in his famous fatwas on wills, where he gave a fatwa of the invalidity of a will for one who recites and gifts the reward to the soul of the testator, and similarly al-Barkawi explicitly ruled its invalidity at the end of al-Tariqah al-Muhammadiyyah. His statement: (And there is not considered in his case what we mentioned, etc.) is clarified by what is in al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah: He was asked about a teacher who died after completing a year as a teacher: does he deserve what is stipulated for the teaching position? He answered: Yes, he deserves the stipulated amount for his work, as stated in Anfa' al-Wasa'il, and al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir followed it. He said in Anfa' al-Wasa'il after quoting references from the author of al-Qunyah: These branches that the author of al-Qunyah mentioned contain what is explicit: that the teacher, the imam, and the muezzin are not considered in their case the time of the crop's emergence, and that is only because these positions have an admixture of hire, because the teacher goes to a specific place, recites, teaches students, and gifts the reward of his recitation to the waqif, and similarly the jurist and the imam. This is not obligatory upon him to do. So the portion he takes is from three installments, as pointed out in Fath al-Qadir, so the installment is divided between them according to service. If you say: Ibn al-Shahnah said, citing al-Ta'liqah in al-Masa'il al-Daqiqah by Ibn al-Sa'igh in his own handwriting: What the jurists take from schools is not a wage because the conditions of hire are not met, nor is it charity because a rich person takes it; rather, it is an assistance for them to devote themselves to study, so that even if they do not attend the lesson due to study and commentary, it is permissible for them to take the stipend. He did not attribute this to a book, but what was recently mentioned from Qadikhan bears witness to it, where he reasoned that writing is part of learning. I say: It is carried upon endowments for jurists without specifying specific days, as we previously mentioned from Ibn al-Shahnah. Hence it is said in al-Qunyah: In Bukhara, endowments for attending lessons for scholars—nothing else is known from the waqif. So the administrator may favor some and deprive others, since the endowment is not for a countable group. Similarly, the endowment for those who come to this school, or for its students, or for its scholars, the administrator may favor some and deprive others if the waqif did not specify what to give each of them. Then he enumerated absolute endowments for jurists. It was said: preference is by need, and it was said: by merit. End quote. If you say: How did al-Tarsusi differentiate between children and positions, while what is explicit in the fatwas contradicts him? He said in al-Bazzaziyyah: The imam of the mosque takes the crop and went before... the endowment that is in return for this work is in the sense of a wage. And it is said in al-Ashbah: If the teacher dies during the year, for example, before the crop comes and before it appears, and he has worked for a period, then dies or is removed, one should look at the time of distributing the crop to the duration of his service and to the service of the one after him, and spread the stipend over the teachers, and see how much is for the separated and the connected teacher, and give him proportionally to his duration, and not consider in his case the time of the crop and its realization, as was considered for the children in the endowment. Rather, the ruling differs between them and the teacher, the jurist, and the holder of any position. This is more appropriate to fiqh and more just. Thus al-Tarsusi edited it in Anfa' al-Wasa'il. And Allah knows best. End quote from al-Khayriyyah. And in it: He was asked about a vineyard endowed upon the children of the waqif; a child died after its blossoms came out and became unripe grapes: Is his share inherited from him, or does it go to the person to whom the endowment reverts after him? He answered: It is inherited from him, because what is meant by the emergence of the crop, its coming, or its arrival in their speech is its becoming of value, as stated in Anfa' al-Wasa'il. There is no doubt that the unripe grapes have value, and they explicitly stated that if he dies after the crop comes out, his share is inherited from him. Rather, his statement in Anfa' al-Wasa'il is that it is inherited even if its ripening has not appeared. He said that after much discussion. Upon this, the arrival of the crop is carried, and the crop comes with the appearance of the plants from the ground and the blossoms from the branches, because they have value on the day they come, generally, as they said regarding the permissibility of selling what has not yet ripened. End quote. And Allah knows best. I say: And with this you know the incorrectness of what the author researched in Jihad in the chapter of spoils, that if the crop comes out and the administrator collects it before division, the share of the entitled person is inherited due to the confirmation of the right; but if before collection in the hands of the trustee, it is not inherited, by analogy to spoils: when they are brought to Dar al-Islam and one of the fighters dies, his share is inherited, but if he dies before that, it is not inherited. And apparently, he does not differentiate between whether the entitled person is like the teacher and imam or from the children, and you have learned the difference between them explicitly in the statement.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, dealing with the nature of stipends (ma'lum) taken by functionaries of waqf endowments, such as teachers (mudarris), imams, and muezzins. The central issue is whether these payments are wages (ujrah), gifts (silah), or charity (sadaqah), and how this affects the timing of entitlement when a functionary dies or is removed before the crop (ghallah) is harvested. The commentator, Zayn al-Din ibn Nujaym, cites al-Tarsusi's Anfa' al-Wasa'il, which analyses the stipend as having a mix (shob) of all three. The ujrah element is applied for considering the period of actual service; the silah element allows the functionary to keep the payment if he dies or is removed after receiving it, without refunding the remainder of the year; and the sadaqah element validates the endowment itself, as endowments are inherently charitable and cannot be made solely for the rich. The key ruling is that for functionaries, entitlement is based on actual service performed, not on the arrival of the crop. Therefore, if a teacher dies mid-year before the crop comes, his stipend should be divided proportionally based on his service time, unlike the case of offspring (awlād) in a family endowment, where entitlement vests when the crop appears (since for them the stipend is pure charity). The commentator also addresses a contrary practice in Cairo where installments are considered, but he affirms Tarsusi's view as more just. Further, he discusses a dispute from Ibn al-Shahna claiming the stipend is not a wage but an assistance (i'ānah), and reconciles it by limiting that to endowments without specified attendance days. The text then applies the same principle to the case of a vineyard endowed on offspring: if a child dies after the grapes have formed (even unripe, hasram), his share is inherited because the crop is considered to have appeared when it has value. Finally, the commentator critiques the author's (i.e., Ibn Nujaym's) earlier discussion in the chapter of Jihad about spoils, where he analogized waqf to spoils regarding inheritance before collection; the commentator shows this analogy is flawed because it does not consider the distinction between functionaries (ujrah-like) and offspring (sadaqah-like). The entire passage illustrates the Hanafi method of ta'līl (reasoning) and tafriq (differentiation) to resolve apparent contradictions.

Key Terms
الغلة (al-ghallah): The produce, revenue, or crop from the waqf property, e.g., rent from land or fruit from trees.
شوب الإجارة (shob al-ijarah): An admixture or resemblance of a hire contract; the stipend has some qualities of a wage without being a full-fledged hire.
المعلوم (al-ma'lum): The fixed stipend or salary assigned to a waqf functionary, known in amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this passage, if a teacher (mudarris) dies mid-year before the waqf crop (ghallah) arrives, how is his stipend (ma'lum) treated?
A) His estate receives nothing because the crop has not yet appeared.
B) His estate receives a proportional share based on the time he actually taught.
C) His estate receives the entire year's stipend because he held the position.
D) His estate receives the full stipend minus a penalty for not completing the term.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi view: a waqf functionary's stipend has an admixture of wage, making entitlement proportional to service time, unlike offspring whose entitlement vests upon crop emergence.

Distribution of Waqf Stipends: Functionaries vs Children
Distinguishing between prorated salary for workers and time-based share for children

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between how waqf stipends are distributed for functionaries (prorated by service) and children (based on appearance of fruit) and apply the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Functionaries are paid for service; children are supported by maintenance—that distinction governs mid-year distribution.

When a waqf recipient dies or leaves mid-year, the distribution of the annual stipend depends on whether they are a functionary (imam, teacher, student) or a child beneficiary. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi distinction between wages (ujra) and maintenance (nafaqa) that underlies the ruling. We will follow the analysis of Ibn Nujaym and the relied-upon view of al-Tarsusi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of waqf recipients
The passage distinguishes between 'arbab al-waza'if' (functionaries like teachers and imams) and 'awlad' (children of the waqf). Note that each receives a stipend from the waqf revenue, but the legal nature differs.
Children's stipend is akin to nafaqah (maintenance); functionaries' stipend is akin to ujrah (wage).
2
Determine the rule for functionaries
For functionaries, the stipend is earned by service. Thus, if a teacher dies or is removed mid-year, his heirs receive only a portion proportional to the period he served. The time of fruit appearance (zuhur al-ghalla) is irrelevant.
This is the view preferred by al-Tarsusi and endorsed in later works.
3
Determine the rule for children
For children, entitlement is based on being alive at the time the fruit appears. If a child dies before fruit appearance, nothing is due; if after, the full share goes to his estate.
This mirrors the rule for maintenance: obligation arises from need at the time of availability.
4
Analyze the opposing view and the tarjih
Some earlier fatwas (e.g., al-Bazzaziyya) suggest that if a functionary received the full stipend upfront, he need not refund any portion if he leaves later. However, al-Tarsusi and later authorities hold that proration is more just and consistent with the wage analogy.
The mufta bihi is the prorated view, as it aligns with qiyas and fairness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت كيف فرق الطرسوسي الأولاد أرباب وبين الوظائف وصريح ما في الفتاوى يخالفه؟ قال في البزازية : إمام المسجد رفع الغلة وذهب قبل مضي السنة لا يسترد منه غلة بعض السنة والعبرة لوقت الحصاد، فإن كان يؤم في وقت الحصاد يستحقه وصار كالجزية وموت الحاكم في خلال السنة وكذا حكم الطلبة في المدارس اهـ . قلت : إن قوله والعبرة لوقت الحصاد إنما هو فيما إذا قبض معلوم السنة بتمامها وذهب قبل مضيها لا لاستحقاقه من غير قبض مع أنه في القنية نقل عن بعض الكتب أنه ينبغي أن يسترد من الإمام حصة ما لم يؤم فيه اهـ. فإن قلت كيف فرق الطرسوسي الأولاد أرباب وبين الوظائف وصريح ما في الفتاوى يخالفه؟ قال في البزازية : إمام المسجد رفع الغلة وذهب قبل مضي السنة لا يسترد منه غلة بعض السنة والعبرة لوقت الحصاد، فإن كان يؤم في وقت الحصاد يستحقه وصار كالجزية وموت الحاكم في خلال السنة وكذا حكم الطلبة في المدارس اهـ . قلت : إن قوله والعبرة لوقت الحصاد إنما هو فيما إذا قبض معلوم السنة بتمامها وذهب قبل مضيها لا لاستحقاقه من غير قبض مع أنه في القنية نقل عن بعض الكتب أنه ينبغي أن يسترد من الإمام حصة ما لم يؤم فيه اهـ. وقال في الأشباه : فإذا مات المدرس في أثناء السنة مثلاً قبل مجيء الغلة وقبل ظهورها وقد باشر مدة ثم مات أو عزل ينبغي أن ينظر وقت قسمة الغلة إلى مدة مباشرته وإلى مباشرة من جاء بعده ويبسط المعلوم على المدرسين وينظر كم يكون للمدرس المنفصل والمتصل فيعطى بحسابه مدته ولا يعتبر في حقه زمان الغلة وإدراكها كما اعتبر في حق الأولاد في الوقف، بل يفترق الحكم بينهم وبين المدرس والفقيه وصاحب وظيفة ما، وهذا هو الأشبه بالفقه والأعدل ؛ كذا حرره الطرسوسي في أنفع الوسائل والله تعالى أعلم اهـ ما في الخيرية
If you say: How did al-Tarsusi distinguish between children and holders of functions, while the explicit content of the fatwas contradicts him? He said in al-Bazzaziyya: The imam of a mosque took the crop and left before the end of the year; he should not have taken back from him the crop of part of the year, and consideration is given to the time of harvest. If he led prayers at the time of harvest, he deserves it, and it becomes like the jizyah and the death of the judge during the year, and similarly the ruling for students in schools. I say: His statement 'consideration is given to the time of harvest' applies only when he had received the full annual stipend and left before its completion, not due to entitlement without receipt, although in al-Qunyah it is transmitted from some books that it is appropriate to take back from the imam the portion for which he did not lead prayers. He said in al-Ashbah: If a teacher dies mid-year, for example, before the arrival of the crop and before its appearance, and he had served for a period then died or was removed, then at the time of dividing the crop, one should look at his period of service and the service of his successor, and the known amount is distributed among the teachers; one sees how much is due to the separated and connected teacher, and he is given proportionally to his period. The time of the crop and its ripening are not considered in his right, as is considered in the right of children in the waqf. Rather, the ruling differs between them and the teacher, the jurist, and any holder of a function. This is more in line with fiqh and more just. Thus al-Tarsusi recorded it in Anfa' al-Wasa'il, and Allah knows best. End of what is in al-Khayriyya.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed Hanafi ruling on how to distribute waqf proceeds among stipend recipients when the recipient dies or leaves mid-year. The key distinction is between children of the waqf (awlad) and functionaries (arbab al-waza'if) such as teachers, imams, and students. For children, entitlement is determined by the time the fruit appears (zuhur al-ghalla) — they inherit based on being alive at that moment, regardless of actual need. For functionaries, the stipend is treated as ujra (wage) for service performed. Therefore, if an imam or teacher serves part of the year, he or his heirs are entitled only to a proportionate share of the annual stipend, not the whole. Al-Tarsusi in Anfa' al-Wasa'il prefers this view as more just, citing al-Ashbah. The text also notes a disagreement: some earlier fatwas and al-Bazzaziyya suggest that if the imam received the full stipend and then left mid-year, he should not repay any portion. However, al-Qunyah reports that he should repay the unused portion. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) reconciles by saying the earlier view applies only when he had physically received the entire stipend upfront. The default principle is that service-based stipends are prorated, and the time of fruit appearance is irrelevant for functionaries. This is a clear application of qiyas: comparing the stipend to wages (ujra) rather than to maintenance (nafaqa).

Key Terms
الغلة (al-ghalla): The produce or revenue of a waqf property, e.g., fruit from a garden or rent from a building.
أرباب الوظائف (arbab al-waza’if): Holders of specific functions in a waqf, such as teacher (mudarris), imam, or student (talib).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The full annual stipend goes to his heirs because he was entitled upon appointment.
B) Only a portion proportional to his actual teaching days up to death.
C) Nothing because he did not live until the fruit appeared.
D) The stipend is forfeited to the waqf.

Key Takeaway
Functionaries are paid wages; children receive maintenance—so mid-year distribution differs: prorated service for functionaries, fruit-appearance timing for children.

Inheriting a Child's Share in Waqf After Fruit Appears
Ruling that after fruit appears, a child's share becomes inheritable, even if unripe

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on when a child's share in a waqf becomes inheritable and explain the basis in the concept of 'appearance of fruit' having market value.

Core Idea
Even unripe grapes have value – once fruit appears, a child's share is inheritable.

In waqf endowments for children, a key question arises: what if a beneficiary dies before the fruit ripens? Does the unripe produce become part of his inheritance? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a fatwa that resolves the issue by defining 'appearance of fruit' as the moment it gains market value, even if unripe. It also corrects a prior misunderstanding that possession by the overseer is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
Consider a vineyard waqf for children; one child dies after flowers appear but before grapes ripen. What is the status of his share?
The fruit at this stage is called hisrim (unripe grapes).
2
Extract the Hanafi ruling
The fatwa answers that the share is inherited from the child, because 'appearance of fruit' in Hanafi usage means the fruit has become valuable, not necessarily ripe.
The key is market value, not ripeness.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The ruling is based on a qiyas khafi: since unripe grapes have value (e.g., for vinegar), they are considered 'appeared' just like ripe fruit. This is confirmed by al-Tarsusi in Anfa' al-Wasa'il.
The analogy is to the permissibility of selling unripe fruit along with the tree.
4
Note the self-correction
The author, Ibn Nujaym, admits his earlier mistake: he had compared waqf to war booty, where possession is required. He now distinguishes children beneficiaries from functionaries.
Children's right vests upon fruit appearance; functionaries' right vests upon service.
5
Apply the broader principle
The principle extends to all crops and fruits: once they emerge from the ground or appear on branches and have any value, the beneficiary's right is established.
This applies to crops, dates, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفيها: سئل في كرم موقوف على أولاد الواقف مات ولد منهم بعد خروج زهره وصيرورته حصرماً، هل حصته ميراث عنه أم لمن آل إليه الوقف بعده؟ أجاب : هي ميراث عنه لأن المراد بطلوع الغلة أو خروجها أو مجيئها في كلامهم صيرورتها ذات قيمة كما صرح به في أنفع الوسائل، ولا شك أن الحصرم له قيمة وقد صرحوا بأنه إذا مات بعد خروج الغلة فحصته ميراث عنه بل كلامه في أنفع الوسائل أنه ميراث ولو لم يبد صلاحه ؛ قاله بعد كلام كثير . فعلى هذا يحمل هلال بء الغلة وتأتي الغلة على ظهور الزرع من الأرض والزهر من الغصون لأن له قيمة يوم تجيء في الجملة كما قالوا في جواز بيع ما لم يبد صلاحه اهـ والله أعلم . قلت : وبهذا تعلم عدم صحة ما بحث المؤلف في الجهاد في باب الغنائم من أنه إن خرجت الغلة وأحرزها الناظر قبل القسمة يورث نصيب المستحق لتأكد الحق فيه، وإن قبل الإحراز في يد المتولي لا يورث قياساً على الغنيمة فإنها إذا أخرجت إلى دار الإسلام ومات أحد المقاتلين يورث نصيبه وإن مات قبل ذلك لا يورث وظاهره أيضاً عدم الفرق بين كون المستحق مثل المدرس والإمام أو من الأولاد وقد علمت الفرق بينهما
And in it: He was asked about a vineyard endowed to the children of the waqif; one of the children died after its flower came out and it became unripe grapes. Is his share an inheritance from him or does it go to the one to whom the waqf reverts? He answered: It is an inheritance from him, because what is meant by 'appearance of the fruit' or 'its emergence' or 'its coming' in their speech is its becoming something of value, as clarified in Anfa' al-Wasa'il. There is no doubt that unripe grapes have value. And they have explicitly stated that if he dies after the fruit appears, his share is an inheritance from him; rather, his statement in Anfa' al-Wasa'il is that it is an inheritance even if its ripeness has not become evident; he said this after much discussion. Upon this is understood the crescent of the fruit, and the fruit applies to the emergence of the crop from the ground and the flower from the branches, because it has value on the day it comes in general, as they said regarding the permissibility of selling what has not yet become ripe. End. And Allah knows best. I say: By this you know the incorrectness of what the author discussed in Jihad, in the chapter on spoils, that if the fruit emerges and the overseer takes possession before division, the share of the beneficiary is inherited due to the strength of the right, but if before taking possession in the hand of the trustee, it is not inherited, by analogy to booty, because if it is brought out to Dar al-Islam and one of the fighters dies, his share is inherited, but if he died before that, it is not inherited. And apparently there is no difference between the beneficiary being like a teacher or imam or from the children, whereas you have known the difference between them.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific inheritance question in waqf: When a child of the waqif dies after the flowers of a vineyard have appeared but before the grapes ripen, does his share of the produce become part of his estate? The ruling from al-Khayriyya is clear: once the fruit has emerged and has commercial value (even as unripe grapes), the share becomes inheritable. The key principle is 'zuhur al-ghalla' — the fruit is considered to have 'appeared' when it has any market value, even if not yet ripe. This is consistent with the Hanafi position on selling unripe produce with the tree. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) uses this to correct a mistake he made earlier in his own work (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) in the book of Jihad, where he suggested that in waqf, the share is inheritable only if the overseer physically takes possession before division, drawing an analogy to war booty. He now realizes the error: for waqf beneficiaries who are children, the rule is different from functionaries; children's shares are inheritable upon appearance of the fruit regardless of possession. This distinction aligns with the previous lesson, where children's entitlement is tied to the time of fruit appearance, not to actual service. The correction shows the importance of distinguishing between types of beneficiaries.

Key Terms
طلوع الغلة (tulu' al-ghalla): The emergence of the crop or fruit to the point where it has market value, even if unripe.
حصرم (hisrim): Unripe grapes that have not yet sweetened but have commercial value (e.g., for vinegar or preservatives).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It goes to the other beneficiaries.
B) It becomes part of his inheritable estate.
C) It reverts to the waqf.
D) It is given to the overseer.

Key Takeaway
A child's share in waqf produce becomes inheritable as soon as the fruit has market value, regardless of ripeness or possession by the overseer.

Substitution (Niyaba) in Waqf Functions: Permissibility and Stipend Rights
Ruling that substitution is permissible for imams and teachers based on custom and fatwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state whether substitution is permissible in waqf functions and explain how the original beneficiary's stipend is affected during a valid absence.

Core Idea
The original functionary keeps his waqf stipend during a valid absence; substitution is permitted by custom even without the waqif's permission.

In this lesson, we examine a practical issue in waqf administration: can the imam, teacher, or repetitor appoint a substitute during illness or Hajj without losing his stipend? The Hanafi school, based on custom and the deductions of later scholars, allows this. We will explore the evidence from al-Khassaf and the fatwa works that support this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Substitution (niyaba) in waqf functions. Ruling: permissible (mubah).
2
Locate the basis
The passage relies on custom (urf) and necessity, deduced from al-Khassaf's statement about a trustee (qayyim) and his stipend during incapacity.
Al-Khassaf's original case involved total vs. partial incapacity.
3
Trace the deduction
Al-Tarsusi extends the ruling from the trustee to all functionaries using qiyas on the level of ability to perform core duties.
The illa is the ability to speak, command, etc.
4
Note the intra-madhhab difference
Earlier scholars considered the harvest season (whoever works then gets stipend); later scholars consider the entire period of service.
The later view is the mufta bihi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The later view, supported by texts in al-Qunyah, al-Khulasah, and Fatawa al-Sayrafiyya, holds that substitution is permissible and the original retains the stipend.
This is based on custom (urf) and the principle 'What the believers consider good is good before Allah.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : هل تجوز النيابة في الوظائف مطلقاً أو يعذر أم لا مطلقاً؟ قلت : لم أر فيها نقلاً عن أصحابنا إلا ما ذكره الطرسوسي في أنفع الوسائل فهماً من كلام الخصاف فإنه قال : قلت أرأيت إن حلت بهذا القيم آفة من الآفات مثل الخرس والعمى وذهاب العقل والفالج وأشباه ذلك هل يكون له الأجر قائماً أم لا؟ قال : إذا حل به من ذلك شيء يمكنه معه الكلام والأمر والنهي فالأجر له قائم، وإن كان لا يمكنه معه الكلام والأمر والنهي والأخذ والإعطاء لم يكن له من هذا الأجر شيء اهـ . قال الطرسوسي : فاستنبطنا منه جواب مسألة واقعة وهي أن المدرس أو الفقية أو المعيد أو الإمام أو من كان مباشراً شيئاً من وظائف المدارس إذا مرض أو حج وحصل له ما يسمونه الناس عذراً شرعياً على اصطلاحهم المتعارف بين الفقهاء أنه لا يحرم مرسومه المعين بل يصرف إليه ولا تكتب عليه غيبة ومقتضى ما ذكره الخصاف أنه لا يستحق شيئاً من المعلوم مدة ذلك العذر فالمدرس إذا مرض أو الفقيه أو أحد من أرباب الوظائف فإنه على ما قال. قوله : قلت إن قوله (الخ أقول : في حواشي الأشباه للحموي ما قاله الطرسوسي قول المتأخرين، وأما قول المتقدمين فالمعتبر وقت الحصاد فمن كان يباشر الوظيفة وقت الحصاد استحق ومن لا فلا . وقد كتب المولى أبو السعود مفتي السلطنة السليمانية رسالة في هذا وحاصلها أن المتقدمين يعتبرون وقت الحصاد والمتأخرين يعتبرون زمن المباشرة والتوزيع. قوله : (قلت لم أر فيها نقلاً الخ) قال العلامة البيري في شرحه على الأشباء والنظائر : رأيت بخط العلامة الشيخ محمد بدر الدين الشهاوي الحنفي المصري : وتجوز الاستنابة وبذلك جرت العادة في الأعصار والأمصار، وما رآه المؤمنون حسناً فهو عند الله حسن، ويشهد لذلك ما ذكر في القنية والخلاصة وفتاوى الصيرفية وغيرها. قال في القنية : استخلف الإمام في المسجد خليفة ليؤم في زمان غيبته لا يستحق الخليفة من أوقاف الإمام شيئاً إن كان الإمام أم أكثر السنة .اهـ. وقال في الخلاصة : إمام الجامع له أن يستخلف وإن لم يؤذن له الاستخلاف ..اهـ وعبارة الصيرفية في الكراهية ما نصه : حانوت وقف على إمام المسجد وغاب ثلاثة أشهر وخلف خليفة يؤمهم ثم حضر فأجرة الحانوت في تلك المدة التي غاب يجوز أخذها أم لا؟ قال : يجوز إن كان هو أو رجل آخر أجر الحانوت بأمره ولكن سبيله التصدق احتياطاً اهـ. منطوق القنية أن الاستنابة جائزة ومن مفهومه أن الغائب يستحق المعلوم وإن لم يكن المستنيب أم أكثر السنة، ومن عبارة الخلاصة جواز الاستنابة مطلقاً، ومن عبارة الصيرفية جوازها
If you say: Is substitution (niyaba) in functions absolutely permissible, or is there an excuse, or absolutely not? I say: I have not seen a transmission from our companions regarding it except what al-Tarsusi mentioned in Anfa' al-Wasa'il, understanding from the words of al-Khassaf, for he said: I said: Do you see if this trustee (qayyim) is struck by some calamity such as dumbness, blindness, loss of mind, paralysis, and the like—does he retain the stipend or not? He said: If he is struck by something with which he can still speak, command, and forbid, then the stipend remains for him. If he cannot speak, command, forbid, take, or give, then he has nothing of this stipend. Al-Tarsusi said: So we derived from it the answer to a real issue: that the teacher (mudarris), the jurist (faqih), the repetitor (mu'id), the imam, or anyone directly performing some function of the schools—if he becomes ill, performs Hajj, or has what people call a valid excuse according to the conventional usage among jurists—then he is not deprived of his usual stipend; rather, it is paid to him and no absence is recorded against him. But the implication of what al-Khassaf mentioned is that he deserves nothing from the stipend during the period of that excuse. So the teacher if ill, or the faqih, or any of the function holders—it is as he said. His statement: I say: his statement etc.: I say: In the commentaries of al-Ashbah by al-Hamawi, what al-Tarsusi said is the view of the later scholars. As for the view of the earlier scholars, consideration is given to the time of harvest; whoever performs the function at harvest time deserves it, and whoever does not does not. And Mawla Abu al-Su'ud, the mufti of the Sulaymaniyya sultanate, wrote a treatise on this; its summary is that the earlier scholars consider the time of harvest, and the later scholars consider the time of performance and distribution. His statement: (I say: I have not seen a transmission etc.) The scholar al-Bayri said in his commentary on al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir: I saw in the handwriting of the scholar Shaykh Muhammad Badr al-Din al-Shihawi al-Hanafi al-Misri: Substitution is permissible, and that is the custom in all ages and regions. What the believers consider good is good before Allah. Witness to this is what is mentioned in al-Qunyah, al-Khulasah, Fatawa al-Sayrafiyya, and others. He said in al-Qunyah: If the imam of a mosque appoints a substitute to lead prayers during his absence, the substitute does not deserve anything from the waqf of the imam if the imam led most of the year. He said in al-Khulasah: The imam of a congregational mosque may appoint a substitute even if he was not given permission to do so. The wording of al-Sayrafiyya on dislike is: A shop endowed to the imam of a mosque; he was absent for three months and appointed a substitute to lead them, then he returned. Is the rent of the shop for that period of absence permissible for him to take? He said: It is permissible if he or another rented the shop by his order, but the proper way is to give it as charity as a precaution. The explicit text of al-Qunyah is that substitution is permissible, and from its implication, the absent person deserves the stipend even if the one who appointed him did not lead most of the year. From the wording of al-Khulasah, substitution is absolutely permissible. From the wording of al-Sayrafiyya, its permissibility...
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage investigates the permissibility of substitution (niyaba) in waqf functions like teaching, leading prayers, etc. The commentator first notes a lack of explicit transmission from early Hanafi authorities, then turns to al-Tarsusi's deduction from al-Khassaf. Al-Khassaf discussed a trustee's entitlement when incapacitated: he retains the stipend if he retains minimal ability, otherwise not. Al-Tarsusi extended this to other functionaries: if a teacher or imam becomes ill or goes for Hajj, he does not lose his stipend based on this analogy. However, later writers note a dispute between earlier and later scholars: earlier scholars tied entitlement to the harvest season (whoever works then gets it), while later scholars consider the entire period of service. Ṭarsusi's view represents the later position. The passage then cites Shihawi and al-Bayri who assert that substitution is permissible as a matter of custom and is supported by texts from al-Qunyah, al-Khulasah, and al-Sayrafiyya. The ruling is that the original functionary retains his stipend during a valid absence, and a substitute may be appointed; the substitute does not take the stipend unless the original was absent for most of the year. This is a practical concession to necessity. The overall message is that niyaba is permitted, and the original beneficiary's entitlement is not lost.

Key Terms
النيابة (al-niyaba): Appointing a substitute to perform the function (e.g., teaching, leading prayers) during one's absence.
المرسوم (al-marsum): The fixed stipend or allocation from the waqf for the functionary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi view (mutā’akhkhirūn), what happens to a teacher’s waqf stipend if he goes for Hajj and appoints a substitute?
A) The substitute gets the stipend.
B) The teacher loses the stipend for that period.
C) The teacher retains the stipend.
D) The stipend is given to charity.

Key Takeaway
Substitution in waqf functions is permissible based on custom; the original beneficiary does not lose his stipend during a valid excuse.

Stipend for Imam Absent Part of the Year
Ruling on stipend refund for imam absent during part of year with early vs late views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on stipend entitlement for an imam who is absent part of the year, identify the criterion used by early scholars, and apply the later view's ruling.

Core Idea
Annual waqf stipend is compensation for actual service; absence without service requires refund.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq explores an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the annual stipend for an imam of a waqf masjid who is absent part of the year. The early Hanafi scholars considered the time of harvest as the criterion for full entitlement, while later scholars tie it to actual days served. Which view is relied upon for fatwa? Let's follow the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
An imam receives an annual stipend (malum) from waqf revenue but is absent for part of the year. The question is whether he must refund any portion.
2
State the early Hanafi position and its analogy
Early scholars (mutqaddimun) consider the time of harvest as the critical point. If the imam led prayers at harvest time, he deserves the full stipend; otherwise, he must refund. They analogize to jizya, which is due for the full year if conditions are met at the start, and to the death of a judge during the year.
The analogy is based on the idea that the service at harvest is the most significant part.
3
State the later Hanafi position and its basis
Later scholars tie entitlement to actual days served. The stipend is compensation for service; therefore, the imam must refund the portion for which he did not lead prayer. This is based on the principle that waqf benefits should match actual benefit received.
4
Note the author's clarification
The author (صاحب البحر الرائق) clarifies that the early view applies only when the imam already received the full year's stipend in advance and then left before the year ended. It does not establish entitlement without receipt.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The later view is generally practiced, especially in Ottoman times, per fatwa of Abu al-Su'ud. This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مضي السنة لا المسجد يسترد منه غلة بعض السنة والعبرة لوقت الحصاد، فإن كان يؤم في وقت الحصاد يستحقه وصار كالجزية وموت الحاكم في خلال السنة وكذا حكم الطلبة في المدارس اهـ . قلت : إن قوله والعبرة لوقت الحصاد إنما هو فيما إذا قبض معلوم السنة بتمامها وذهب قبل مضيها لا لاستحقاقه من غير قبض مع أنه في القنية نقل عن بعض الكتب أنه ينبغي أن يسترد من الإمام حصة ما لم يؤم فيه اهـ.
The passing of the year does not [affect the masjid?]; he is reclaimed from the produce of part of the year, and the consideration is at the time of harvest. If he led prayer at harvest time, he deserves it, and it is like the jizya and the death of the judge during the year, and similarly the ruling for students in schools. I say: His statement 'consideration at harvest time' is only when he received the stipend for the full year and then left before its expiry, not because he deserves it without receipt. Moreover, in al-Qunyah it is transmitted from some books that the imam should be made to refund the portion for which he did not lead prayer.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on an imam appointed to a waqf who receives an annual stipend (malum) but is absent for part of the year. The early scholars (mutqaddimun) consider the time of harvest as the criterion: if the imam performed his duties at harvest time, he gets the full stipend; if not, he must refund the portion for the time he missed. This is analogous to jizya being due per year, and the death of a judge during the year not entitling his heirs to the full year's salary. The author (صاحب البحر الرائق) clarifies that this applies only when the imam already received the full year's stipend and then left before the year ended; it is not about entitlement without receipt. He then cites from al-Qunyah that some books recommend the imam refund the amount for the days he did not lead. This reflects the difference between early and late Hanafi scholars: late scholars tie entitlement to actual service throughout the year, not just harvest time.

Key Terms
غلة (ghalla): Produce or revenue from waqf, used to pay stipends.
معلوم (malum): Fixed stipend for a waqf functionary, usually paid annually.
عبرة (ibrah): Consideration or criterion for determining entitlement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He does not need to refund anything.
B) He must refund the portion for the time he missed.
C) He only needs to refund if he missed the harvest time.
D) He can keep the stipend if he appointed a substitute.

Key Takeaway
Annual waqf stipend for an imam is compensation for actual days served; refund is required for periods of absence without service.

Deputization in Waqf Functions: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Dispute on permissibility of deputization (niyaba) for waqf functionaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two major Hanafi positions on deputization (niyaba) for waqf functionaries and identify the conditions under which each view applies.

Core Idea
Deputization in waqf is contested: some Hanafi authorities permit it with conditions, while others forbid it entirely based on al-Khassaf's reasoning.

This lesson explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi debate over whether a waqf functionary such as an imam or teacher may appoint a deputy during absence. Some early authorities, distilled by al-Tarsusi from al-Khassaf, argue that the stipend is tied to personal service and deputization is never allowed. However, later texts like al-Qunyah and al-Khulasah permit it, citing custom and the principle that 'what believers see as good is good with Allah.' Understanding this dispute requires careful attention to the distinction between permanent disability and temporary excuses, and to the operative fatwa for practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing positions
State clearly that there is a view that deputization is never permitted (derived from al-Khassaf) and a view that it is permitted with conditions (from al-Qunyah, al-Khulasah, al-Sirafiyyah, and others).
2
Trace the authority chain for each position
For the impermissibility position: al-Tarsusi's inference from al-Khassaf's ruling on a permanently disabled custodian. For permissibility: explicit statements in al-Qunyah, al-Khulasah, and Fatawa al-Sirafiyyah, supported by custom.
Al-Khassaf's case involves permanent total disability, not temporary absence.
3
Analyze the key distinction: permanent vs. temporary
Al-Khassaf's ruling applies to a qayyim who is completely unable to perform functions permanently. The permissive authorities consider temporary excuses like illness or Hajj as valid grounds for deputization, allowing the original to retain the stipend under certain conditions.
This distinction resolves the apparent contradiction.
4
Determine the operative fatwa (mufta bihi)
Later Hanafi practice, as recorded by Abu al-Su'ud and al-Biri, favors permissibility with conditions: the deputy does not receive from the waqf unless the original served most of the year; the original may receive the stipend only if he personally arranges it and does not double-dip.
5
Apply to a concrete scenario
Consider a teacher at a waqf school who goes for Hajj for two months. Under the permissive view, he may appoint a qualified teacher as deputy, and his stipend continues if he arranged it. Under the strict view, he would forfeit the stipend for that period.
The fatwa today follows the permissive view.

If you say: Is deputization allowed absolutely, or with an excuse, or not at all? I say: I have not seen a transmission from our companions except what al-Tarsusi mentioned in Anfa' al-Wasa'il, understanding from the speech of al-Khassaf. He said: Do you see if this custodian is afflicted with an affliction such as muteness, blindness, insanity, paralysis and the like, is his wage ongoing or not? He said: If he is afflicted with something that still allows him to speak, command, and forbid, then his wage is ongoing; if he is unable to speak, command, forbid, take, and give, then he has nothing of this wage. Al-Tarsusi said: We derived from this the answer to a real issue: a teacher, a jurist, a reiterator, an imam, or anyone directly involved in a function in schools if he falls ill, goes on Hajj, and obtains what people call a legal excuse, according to the conventional usage among jurists, that his fixed stipend is not forfeited but is given to him and no absence is recorded against him. However, the implication of what al-Khassaf mentioned is that he does not deserve anything of the stipend during that excuse. So the teacher if ill, or the jurist, or any of the function holders, is as he said. His statement: I say his statement... I say: In the hawashi of al-Ashbah by al-Hamawi, what al-Tarsusi said is the view of the later scholars; as for the view of the early scholars, the consideration is the time of harvest. Whoever directly performed the function at harvest time deserves, and whoever did not does not. Mawla Abu al-Su'ud, the mufti of the Sulaymaniyya sultanate, wrote a treatise on this, the summary of which is that the early scholars consider the harvest time, and the later scholars consider the time of direct service and distribution. His statement: I say I have not seen a transmission... Al-Biri said in his commentary on al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir: I saw in the handwriting of the scholar Shaykh Muhammad Badr al-Din al-Shihawi al-Hanafi al-Misri: Deputization is allowed, and custom has continued in all ages and regions; what the believers see as good is good with Allah. This is supported by what is mentioned in al-Qunyah, al-Khulasah, Fatawa al-Sirafiyyah, and others. In al-Qunyah: An imam appointed a deputy in the mosque to lead prayer during his absence; the deputy does not deserve anything from the imam's endowments if the imam led more than half the year. In al-Khulasah: The imam of a congregational mosque may appoint a deputy even if permission is not given. The wording of al-Sirafiyyah on dislike: A shop is a waqf for the imam of a mosque; he was absent for three months and appointed a deputy to lead them; then he returned. Is the rent of the shop from that period permissible for him to take? He said: permissible if he or another man rented out the shop by his order, but its way is to give it in charity as a precaution. The explicit meaning of al-Qunyah is that deputization is allowed, and from its implication that the absent one deserves the stipend even if the deputy did not lead most of the year; from the wording of al-Khulasah, permissibility of deputization absolutely; from the wording of al-Sirafiyyah, permissibility with condition. We derived from this that al-Khassaf's view: If he can directly perform it, he deserves; if he cannot, he deserves nothing of the stipend. He did not consider these contingencies as an excuse that prevents him from his fixed stipend; rather, he made the ruling depend on actual service. So if service exists, he deserves the stipend; if not, he has no stipend. We also derived from this research another answer: Deputization is not allowed, whether with an excuse or without, because al-Khassaf did not permit him to appoint a deputy even with the excuses he mentioned. If deputization were allowed, he would have said: And he may appoint someone to take his place until his excuse is removed. This is also apparent from the evidence and is good fiqh.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage addresses a key question in waqf fiqh: may a functionary (imam, teacher, etc.) appoint a deputy (niyaba) to perform his duties during his absence? The author presents a complex intra-Hanafi debate. Al-Tarsusi quotes al-Khassaf's ruling on a permanently disabled custodian (qayyim): if he can still do some work, his pay continues; if not, it stops. Al-Tarsusi then applies this to temporary excuses like illness or Hajj, concluding that if the person cannot perform the service, he does not deserve the stipend for that period. This implies that deputization is not valid because the original would still be paid if he had appointed a deputy. However, other authorities like al-Qunyah, al-Khulasah, and al-Sirafiyyah explicitly permit deputization, though with conditions: the deputy does not receive from the waqf if the original served most of the year, and the stipend may still go to the original except by private arrangement. The author then synthesizes: al-Khassaf's case is of permanent total disability; temporary absences are different. The fatwa of Abu al-Su'ud distinguishes functions that inherently require personal service (like learning) from those that allow delegation (like teaching and ifta), permitting deputization with a valid excuse.

Key Terms
نيابة / استنابة (niyaba / istinaba): Deputization; appointment of a substitute to perform waqf functions.
عذر شرعي (udhr shar'i): A legally recognized excuse such as illness, Hajj, or travel that prevents direct service.
قيم (qayyim): Custodian or supervisor of a waqf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The permissive view relies on the Quran while al-Khassaf relied on custom.
D) The dispute is only about imams, not teachers.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi waqf law, deputization of functionaries is permitted under conditions, based on custom and later authorities, while acknowledging a strict view that ties stipend to personal service.

Stipend Rights When a Waqf Functionary Appoints a Deputy
Ruling on stipend for imam's deputy in waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who receives the waqf stipend when an imam appoints a deputy, and explain the conditions under which the deputy is entitled to the stipend.

Core Idea
A waqf stipend follows actual service, but valid deputization with a legal excuse transfers it to the deputy.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical waqf issue: if an imam appoints someone to lead prayer during his absence, who receives the stipend? The text reviews multiple Hanafi opinions—from al-Khassaf, al-Qunyah, Ibn Wahban, and finally Abu al-Su'ud—and settles on a detailed rule that balances the waqf's interest with legitimate excuses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Determine who is entitled to the waqf stipend when the original functionary appoints a deputy: the original or the deputy?
The dispute arises from differing views on whether stipend is tied to direct service or can be transferred via deputization.
2
Examine al-Qunyah's ruling
Al-Qunyah states that if the imam served most of the year, the deputy deserves nothing; the original gets the full stipend.
This implies the stipend is based on the original's service record, not the deputy's work.
3
Reconcile with al-Khassaf
Al-Khassaf's stricter view (stipend only for actual service) is reconciled by distinguishing permanent disability from temporary absence with a deputy.
Al-Khassaf's case involves a custodian who is permanently unable to serve; al-Qunyah deals with temporary absence with a replacement.
4
Apply Abu al-Su'ud's fatwa
Abu al-Su'ud rules that deputization is valid only with a legal excuse and if the deputy is equally or more capable; then the full stipend goes to the deputy, not the original.
This is the mufta bihi (operative ruling) adopted by later authorities.
5
Note the practical consequence
The key condition is the presence of a valid legal excuse (e.g., Hajj, illness) and the deputy's competence. Without these, the original retains the stipend.
The ruling protects the waqf's purpose by ensuring service continues without loss of stipend to the actual performer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقدمنا عن ابن وهبان أنه إذا سافر للحج أو صلة الرحم لا ينعزل ولا يستحق المعلوم مع أنهما فرضان عليه وإلا ما ذكره في القنية استخلف الإمام خليفة في المسجد ليؤم فيه زمان غيبته لا يستحق الخليفة من أوقاف الإمامة شيئاً إن كان الإمام أم أكثر السنة .اهـ. وحاصله أن النائب لا يستحق من الوقف شيئاً لأن الاستحقاق بالتقرير ولم يوجد ويستحق الأصيل الكل إن عمل أكثر السنة، وسكت عما إذا لم يعمل أكثر السنة. قوله : (وإلا ما ذكره في القنية) معطوف على قوله إلا ما ذكره الطرسوسي» قال الرملي وفي القنية في باب الإمامة : إمام يترك الإمامة لزيارة أقربائه في الرساتيق أسبوعاً أو نحوه أو المصيبة أو لاستراحة لا بأس به ومثله عفو العادة والشرع اهـ. وقد نقله عنه الشارح في الأشباه في بحث العادة محكمة. والحاصل أن مقتضى كلام الخصاف يخالف مقتضى كلام القنية، وأنت على علم أن كلامه لا يصادم كلام الخصاف ولذلك نص ابن وهبان أنه يسقط معلوم من حج مدة غيبته تأمل .اهـ. قلت: قد يقال إن كلام الخصاف في القيم إذا أصابه شيء من تلك الآفات التي تمنعه عن القيام بما نصب لأجله بالكلية، وما في القنية ليس كذلك، وقد مر عن البزازية أنه لو خرج أقل من خمسة عشر يوماً من غير سفر لأمر لا بد له منه فهو عفو تأمل. ثم إن ما في القنية المذكور في الأشباه حمله الشيخ إبراهيم الحلبي في شرح منية المصلي على ما إذا كان الترك المذكور في سنة خلافاً لما ذكره المؤلف في الأشباه من قوله يسامح في كل شهر أسبوعاً الخ إذ ليس في القنية ما يفيده. قوله : (وحاصله أن النائب لا يستحق الخ) أقول قال العلامة البيري بعد العبارة التي نقلناها عنه آنفاً ما نصه وسئل مفتي الروم مولانا العلامة أبو السعود العمادي رحمه الله تعالى عن الاستنابة فأجاب : الاستنابة إن كانت فيما لا يقبلها أصلاً كطلب العلم وإقرائه فلا يشتبه بطلانها على أحد، وإن كانت فيما يقبلها كالتدريس والإفتاء ونظائرهما، فإن كانت بعذر شرعي وكان النائب في إقامة الخدم مثل الأصل وخيراً منه فهي جائزة إلى يزول ما اعتراه من العذر خلا أن المعلوم بتمامه يكون للنائب ليس للأصيل ، شيء إلا أن يتبرع به النائب عن طيب نفس منه ورضا كامل لا يحوم حوله شيء من الخوف والحياء وهيهات اهـ. وأفتى شيخ مشايخنا القاضي علي بن جار الله الحنفي بجواز النيابة بشرط العذر الشرعي. أقول: والحق التفصيل كما أفتى به مولانا أبو السعود والله أعلم . اهـ كلام البيري رحمه الله تعالى فتأمل. وقد أفتى البحر الرائق ج ٥/ ٢٥٥ أن معه
We have previously mentioned from Ibn Wahban that if he travels for Hajj or maintaining family ties, he is not dismissed but does not deserve the stipend, despite both being obligations upon him. Otherwise, what is mentioned in al-Qunyah: An imam appointed a deputy in the mosque to lead prayer during his absence; the deputy does not deserve anything from the waqf of the imam if the imam led most of the year. Its summary: The deputy does not deserve anything from the waqf because entitlement comes from direct service, which is absent; the original deserves all if he worked most of the year, and he was silent about the case when he did not work most of the year. His statement: (And otherwise what is mentioned in al-Qunyah) is connected to his statement 'except what al-Tarsusi mentioned'. Al-Ramli said: In al-Qunyah, in the chapter on imamate: An imam who leaves the imamate to visit relatives in the rural areas for a week or so, or for a calamity, or for rest, there is no harm, and it is analogous to what is excused by custom and law. The commentator in al-Ashbah transmitted this from him in the discussion of custom being authoritative. The conclusion: The implication of al-Khassaf's speech contradicts the implication of al-Qunyah's speech, and you know that his speech does not contradict al-Khassaf's speech, and therefore Ibn Wahban explicitly stated that the stipend of one who performs Hajj falls during the period of his absence, ponder. I say: It may be said that al-Khassaf's speech is about the custodian when he is afflicted with something that permanently prevents him from performing what he was appointed for, and what is in al-Qunyah is not like that. It has already passed from al-Bazzaziyya that if he goes out for less than fifteen days without travel for a necessary purpose, it is excusable, ponder. Then, what is in al-Qunyah mentioned in al-Ashbah was interpreted by Shaykh Ibrahim al-Halabi in his commentary on Munyat al-Musalli to apply when the abandonment in question is within a year, contrary to what the author mentioned in al-Ashbah from his statement 'he is excused every month a week' etc., since al-Qunyah does not indicate that. His statement: (Summary: the deputy does not deserve) I say: Al-Biri said after the statement we quoted from him: The mufti of Rum, our master the scholar Abu al-Su'ud al-Imadi, may Allah have mercy on him, was asked about deputization and answered: If deputization is in something that does not accept it at all, like seeking knowledge and teaching it, then its invalidity is not unclear to anyone. If it is in something that accepts it, like teaching, giving fatwa, and their likes, then if it is with a legal excuse and the deputy is equal to the original in performing the services or better than him, it is permissible until the excuse is removed, except that the entire stipend goes to the deputy, not the original, unless the deputy donates it willingly with full consent, free from any fear or shyness, which is rare. The teacher of our teachers, Judge Ali ibn Jarallah al-Hanafi, gave a fatwa allowing deputization with a legal excuse. I say: The truth is the detail as given by our master Abu al-Su'ud, and Allah knows best. This is the speech of al-Biri, may Allah have mercy on him, so ponder. And al-Bahr al-Ra'iq gave a fatwa in volume 5, page 255, that with [him?]...
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage resolves the practical question: when an imam or teacher appoints a deputy, who gets the stipend? The author cites Ibn Wahban's ruling that an imam who travels for Hajj loses his stipend for that period, though he does not lose his position. Al-Qunyah adds that if the imam appointed a deputy and served more than half the year, the deputy gets nothing from the waqf; the original gets full stipend. The author reconciles the apparent contradiction between al-Khassaf (who seems to deny any stipend for absence) and al-Qunyah (who allows it with deputization) by distinguishing cases: al-Khassaf deals with permanent disability, while al-Qunyah addresses temporary absence with a deputy. The final fatwa from Abu al-Su'ud provides a comprehensive ruling: deputization is only allowed in functions that accept delegation (like teaching and ifta, not the pursuit of knowledge itself), provided there is a valid legal excuse and the deputy is equally or more capable; in such cases, the entire stipend goes to the deputy, not the original, unless the deputy gifts it. This becomes the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).

Key Terms
أصيل (asil): The original holder of a waqf function, as opposed to the deputy (na'ib).
نائب (na'ib): Deputy appointed to perform functions of the original.
معلوم (malum): Fixed stipend from waqf for a functionary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa of Abu al-Su'ud quoted by al-Biri, who receives the stipend when a waqf functionary appoints a deputy with a valid legal excuse and the deputy is equally capable?
A) The original functionary always keeps the stipend.
B) The deputy receives the entire stipend unless he voluntarily gives it to the original.
C) The stipend is forfeited to the waqf.
D) The stipend is split equally between original and deputy.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi waqf law, when a functionary appoints a deputy with a valid legal excuse and the deputy is equally capable, the stipend belongs entirely to the deputy.

Deputization and Stipend in Waqf: Resolving an Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on deputization in waqf and stipend entitlement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the conflicting Hanafi views on deputization in waqf functions and state the mufta bihi position on stipend entitlement.

Core Idea
Deputization in waqf is permissible with a valid excuse; the deputy, not the principal, receives the stipend.

Hanafi scholars differed on whether a waqf functionary may appoint a deputy and whether the stipend continues during absence. This lesson traces the dispute from al-Khassaf's strict position to later refinements, culminating in the operative fatwa of Abu al-Su'ud. You will learn when deputization is allowed and who is entitled to the stipend.

Guided Path
1
State al-Khassaf's position
Al-Khassaf ruled that a waqf trustee must personally perform duties to deserve the stipend. No deputization allowed, even with excuse.
This is the stricter view.
2
Identify the apparent contradiction in al-Qunyah
Al-Qunyah's passage allows an imam to leave for a week and keep the stipend, suggesting flexibility.
Note the difference: al-Qunyah deals with brief absences.
3
Read the reconciliation by later scholars
Later scholars harmonize by interpreting al-Khassaf's ruling as applying to total permanent inability, while al-Qunyah addresses temporary customary absences.
The key distinction: duration and extent of inability.
4
Examine Abu al-Su'ud's detailed fatwa
Abu al-Su'ud distinguishes functions: personal acts (learning) no deputization; delegable acts (teaching, fatwa) allowed with valid excuse, and the deputy gets the full stipend.
This becomes the relied-upon view.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The author and later scholars adopt Abu al-Su'ud's detail as the operative rule.
Mufta bihi: deputization allowed with valid excuse; deputy entitled to stipend.

مقتضى كلام الخصاف يخالف مقتضى كلام القنية، وأنت على علم أن كلامه لا يصادم كلام الخصاف ولذلك نص ابن وهبان أنه يسقط معلوم من حج مدة غيبته تأمل .اهـ. قلت: قد يقال إن كلام الخصاف في القيم إذا أصابه شيء من And this is that al-Khassaf: if he is able to personally undertake that, he deserves, and if he cannot personally undertake that, he does not deserve anything from the stipend. And he did not make these hindrances an excuse in preventing him from his fixed stipend, but rather made the ruling on the stipend dependent on personal performance: if it exists, he deserves the stipend; if it does not exist, he has no stipend of fiqh. And we also extracted from this research and exposition the answer to another issue: deputization is not permissible, whether with or without excuse, for al-Khassaf did not allow him to deputize despite the excuses he mentioned. And if deputization were permissible, he would have said: and he appoints someone to stand in his place until his excuse ends. And this is also apparent from the evidence, and it is good fiqh. End. And we earlier cited from Ibn Wahban that if he travels for Hajj or maintaining family ties, he is not removed nor does he deserve the stipend, even though both obligations are upon him—unless what is mentioned in al-Qunyah: the imam appoints a khalifa in the mosque to lead prayer during his absence; the khalifa does not deserve anything from the endowments of the imamate if the imam led most of the year. End. Its summary is: the deputy does not deserve anything from the endowment because entitlement is by appointment, and it does not exist; the principal deserves all if he worked most of the year. End. And the commentator transmitted it in al-Ashbah in the discussion of custom as authoritative. His statement: (And its summary is that the deputy does not deserve, etc.) I say: al-Allama al-Birri said after the passage we quoted from him previously, verbatim: The mufti of Rum, our master al-Allama Abu al-Su'ud al-Imadi, may Allah have mercy on him, was asked about deputization and he answered: Deputization, if it is in something that does not accept it at all like seeking knowledge and teaching it, then no one is in doubt about its invalidity. And if it is in something that accepts it, like teaching, giving fatwa, and their likes, then if it is with a legitimate excuse and the deputy is like the principal in performing the service or better than him, it is permissible until the excuse besetting him ends, except that the entire stipend goes to the deputy; the principal has nothing unless the deputy voluntarily gives it with full inner satisfaction and complete consent, not tinged with any fear or shyness—and how rare is that! End. And our shaykh's shaykh, al-Qadi Ali ibn Jarallah al-Hanafi, gave a fatwa permitting deputization on condition of a legitimate excuse. I say: The correct view is the detail as given by our master Abu al-Su'ud, and Allah knows best. End of al-Birri's words, may Allah have mercy on him. Reflect.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding deputization (istiaba) in waqf functions and its effect on the stipend (ma'lum). The author begins by presenting the position of al-Khassaf: a trustee (qayyim) deserves his stipend only if he personally performs the duties. Hindrances do not excuse him; he loses the stipend if unable to perform. Moreover, al-Khassaf does not permit the trustee to appoint a deputy, even with a valid excuse. The author then cites Ibn Wahban's view that a trustee traveling for Hajj or family ties does not lose his position but does not deserve the stipend during absence. Next, al-Qunyah is mentioned, which allows an imam to leave for a week and not lose the stipend, seemingly contradicting al-Khassaf. The author reconciles by noting that al-Khassaf's ruling applies to total inability, while al-Qunyah deals with brief, customary absences. Later, Abu al-Su'ud's detailed fatwa is quoted: deputization is invalid in personal acts like learning/teaching; in delegable acts like teaching and fatwa, it is permissible with a valid excuse, but the deputy gets the full stipend. Al-Birri and Qadi Ali ibn Jarallah confirm this. The author concludes that the correct view is the detailed one: deputization is permissible with a legitimate excuse, and the deputy is entitled to the stipend. This is a classical Hanafi discussion balancing the condition of personal service with practical necessities.

Key Terms
الاستنابة (al-istiaba): The appointment of a substitute or deputy to perform a waqf function in place of the original appointee.
المعلوم (al-ma'lum): The fixed stipend or salary from waqf revenues allocated to the functionary.
القيم (al-qayyim): The trustee or caretaker of a waqf, responsible for its management and supervision.
الناظر بالشرط (al-nazir bi al-shart): A supervisor appointed by the waqif (endower) with a specific condition in the waqf deed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this passage, what happens to the stipend when a waqf functionary appoints a deputy due to a valid excuse?
A) The principal keeps the full stipend.
B) The deputy gets the full stipend.
C) The stipend is divided equally between principal and deputy.
D) The stipend is forfeited.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, deputization in waqf functions is permissible with a valid excuse for delegable tasks, and the deputy is entitled to the stipend.

Deputizing in Religious Posts and Rules for the Waqf Trustee
Ruling on deputizing and trustee rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on deputizing in religious positions and identify the conditions and rules for trustee appointment in waqf.

Core Idea
Deputizing is permissible; the trustee's authority depends on the founder's stipulation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses two key questions in waqf law: can a religious office holder hire a paid deputy, and what are the rules for appointing a trustee? The author, Ibn Nujaym, navigates intra-Hanafi differences and later scholarly consensus to provide the operative rulings. By studying this, you will understand the flexibility of the Hanafi school in adapting to practical needs while adhering to the founder's conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on deputizing
Find the Hanafi position on hiring a deputy for imamate, teaching, or Quran instruction. Is it permissible? On what basis?
The text distinguishes between earlier and later views; the mufta bihi is permissibility.
2
Understand salary entitlement
Examine the scenario where the principal works, the deputy works, or only the deputy works. Who gets the salary? When is the position considered vacant?
Pay attention to the condition of the deputy actually performing the work.
3
Analyze the trustee appointment
State the rules for appointing a trustee by the founder's condition vs. by the judge. What happens after the founder's death?
Abu Yusuf's view is relied upon in waqf matters.
4
Apply rules to multi-trustee scenarios
Understand cases where multiple trustees are appointed, how they share authority, and when the judge intervenes.
The founder's stipulations govern the division of authority.
5
Consider the dispute on salary cutting
Evaluate the disagreement with Imam al-Subki on whether the trustee can cut salary based solely on the attendance clerk's report.
The text does not provide a final Hanafi ruling on this specific point.
