الخلاصة
يعينه الأصيل للنائب كل شهر في مقابلة عمله هل يستحقه النائب عليه أو لا، والظاهر أنه يستحقه لأنها إجارة وقد وفى العمل بناء على قول المتأخرين المفتى به من جواز الاستئجار على الإمامة والتدريس وتعليم القرآن وعلى هذا إذا لم يعمل الأصيل وعمل النائب كان الوظيفة شاغرة ولا يجوز للناظر الصرف إلى واحد منهما ويجوز للقاضي عزله، وعمل الناس بالقاهرة على جواز الاستنابات في الوظائف وعدم اعتبارها شاغرة مع وجود النيابة . ثم رأيت في من كتاب القضاء أن الإمام يجوز استخلافه بلا إذن بخلاف القاضي، وعلى هذا لا تكون وظيفته شاغرة وتصح النيابة ومما يرد على الطرسوسي أن الخصاف صرح بأن للقيم أن يوكل وكيلاً يقوم مقامه وله أن يجعل له من معلومه شيئاً، وكذا في الإسعاف وهذا كالتصريح بجواز الاستنابة لأن النائب وكيل بالأجرة كما لا يخفى فالذي تحرر جواز الاستنابة في الوظائف. فإن قلت : هل للناظر قطع معلوم صاحب الوظيفة بقول كاتب الغيبة وحده مع دعوى المستحق حضوره؟ قلت: لم أر فيها نقلاً لأصحابنا وإنما ذكره الإمام السبكي في فتاواه أنه لا يجوز القطع بقول كاتب الغيبة وحده، وصرح بأنه لا يحل لكاتب الغيبة أن يكتب عليه حتى يعلم أن غيبته كانت لغير عذر لكن هذا مبني على مذهبه من أن الغيبة لعذر لا توجب الحرمان، وأما على ما قدمناه من عدم الاستحقاق فلا، وسيأتي شيء من أحكام الوظائف في بيان تصرفات الناظر إن شاء الله تعالى الموضع الثاني في الناظر بالشرط قدمنا أن الولاية للواقف ثابتة مدة حياته وإن لم يشترطها وأن له عزل المتولي، وأن من ولاه لا يكون له النظر بعد موته إلا بالشرط على قول أبي يوسف ولو نصب الواقف عند موته وصياً ولم يذكر من أمور الوقف شيئاً تكون ولاية الوقف إلى الوصي ولو جعله وصياً في أمر الوقف فقط كان الشيخ خير الدين الرملي بما ذكره المؤلف هنا قوله : (وعلى هذا قال الرملي : أي على القول بعدم جواز الاستنابة. قوله : (للقيم أن يوكل وكيلاً الخ) قال الرملي : ستأتي أيضاً مسألة توكيل القيم في آخر شرح هذه المقولة اهـ. وقال في فتاواه الخيرية بعد نقل حاصل كلام المؤلف هنا : والمسألة وضع فيها رسائل ويجب العمل بما عليه الناس وخصوصاً مع قيام العذر وعلى ذلك جميع المعلوم للمستنيب وليس للنائب إلا الأجرة التي استأجره بها في مدة إنابته عنه لا غير واستحقاقه الأجرة لكونه وفى العمل الذي استأجره عليه فيها، وذلك بناء على ما قاله المتأخرون وعليه الفتوى أن الاستئجار على الإمامة والتدريس وتعليم القرآن جائز .اهـ قوله : (لم أر فيها نقلاً لأصحابنا الخ) تقدم أن الناظر لو أنكر ملازمته فالقول قول المدرس بيمينه وكذا لو مات واختلف مع ورثته فالقول للورثة مع يمينهم، وكذا كل وظيفة القول قوله بيمينه في المباشرة إلى آخر ما قدمناه عن الرملي في المسألة السادسة من المسائل العشرين قوله : (قدمنا) أي قبل ثلاثة أوراق قوله : وقال أبو يوسف يجوز) قال في أنفع الوسائل : وينبغي أن يكون الفتوى عليه إما لأنه أخذ بالاستحسان والأصل أنه مقدم على الوقف
۳۸۷
وصياً في الأشياء كلها عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد خلافاً لأبي يوسف وهلال، وليس لأحد الناظرين التصرف بغير رأي الآخر، وعلى قياس قول أبي يوسف يجوز. ولو أوصى أحدهما الآخر عند موته كان للباقي الانفراد، ولو شرط أن لا يوصي به المتولي عند موته امتنع الإيصاء. ولو جعلها الرجلين فقبل أحدهما ورد الآخر ضم القاضي إلى من قبل رجلاً أو فوض للقابل بمفرده، ولو جعلها لفلان إلى أن يدرك ولدي فإذا أدرك كان شريكاً له لا يجوز ما جعله لابنه في رواية الحسن. وقال أبو يوسف يجوز ولو أوصى إلى رجل بأن يشتري بمال سماه أرضاً ويجعلها وقفاً سماها له وأشهد على وصيته جاز ويكون متولياً وله الإيصاء به لغيره، ولو نصب متولياً على وقفه ثم وقف وقفاً آخر ولم يجعل له متولياً لا يكون متولي الأول متولياً على الثاني إلا بأن يقول أنت وصبي. ولو وقف أرضين وجعل لكل متولياً لا يشارك أحدهما الآخر، ولو جعل ولاية وقفه لرجل ثم جعل رجلاً آخر وصيه يكون شريكاً للمتولي في أمر الوقف إلا أن يقول وقفت أرضي على كذا وكذا وجعلت ولايتها لفلان وجعلت فلاناً وصياً في تركاتي وجميع أموري، فحينئذ ينفرد كل منهما بما فوض إليه ؛ كذا في الإسعاف. ومنه يعلم جواب حادثة وجد مكتوبان شهد أحدهما بأن المتولي فلان وشهد الآخر بأن المتولي تقدم رجل غيره والثاني متأخر التاريخ، فأجبت بأنهما يشتركان ولا يقال إن الثاني ناسخ كما الخصاف في الشرائط لأنا نقول : إن التولية من الواقف خارجة عن حكم سائر الشرائط عن لأن له فيها التغيير والتبديل كلما بدا له من غير شرط في عقدة الوقف على قول أبي يوسف، وأما باقي الشرائط فلا بد من ذكرها في أصل الوقف. ثم قال في الإسعاف : ولو جعل الولاية لأفضل أولاده وكانوا في الفضل سواء تكون لأكبرهم سناً ذكراً كان أو أنثى ولو قال الأفضل فالأفضل من أولادي فأبي أفصلهم القبول أو مات يكون لمن يليه فيه وهكذا على الترتيب ؛ كذا ذكر الخصاف. وقال هلال : القياس أن يدخل القاضي بدله رجلاً ما كان حياً فإذا مات صارت الولاية إلى الذي يليه في الفضل، ولو كان الأفضل غير موضع أقام القاضي رجلاً يقوم بأمر الوقف ما دام الأفضل حياً، فإذا مات ينتقل إلى من يليه فيه، فإذا صار أهلاً بعد ذلك ترد الولاية إليه، وهكذا الحكم لو لم يكن فيهم أحد أهلاً لها فإن القاضي يقيم بما عدا القياس إلا في مسائل ليس هذه منها، وإما لأن الفتوى في الوقف على قول أبي يوسف ثم بحث أن ناظر الوقف كذلك وتمامه فيه فراجعه قوله : ( فحينئذ ينفرد كل منهما بما فوض إليه) لعل وجهه أن أمر الوقف ليس من أمور الواقف فلا يشمله قوله في تركاتي وجميع أموري فكان تخصيصاً الوقف فلا يشارك الأول بخلاف الصورة الأولى فإن الوصاية فيها مطلقة تأمل. قوله: (كما تقدم عن الخصاف) أي قبل هذا بخمسة أوراق من أنه لو شرط أن لا تباع ثم قال في آخره على أن له الاستبدال كان له لأن الثاني ناسخ للأول. قوله : ( ولو كان الأفضل غير موضع) أي غير قادر على
Book of Waqf. Al-Khulasa: The principal assigns to the deputy each month in exchange for his work: does the deputy deserve it from him or not? The apparent is that he deserves it because it is a hire and he has fulfilled the work, based on the saying of the later scholars, which is the fatwa, of the permissibility of hiring for imamate, teaching, and Quran instruction. And on this, if the principal did not work and the deputy worked, the position is vacant, and it is not permissible for the trustee to pay to either of them, and it is permissible for the judge to dismiss him. And the practice of the people in Cairo is on the permissibility of deputizing in positions and not considering them vacant with the existence of deputyship. Then I saw in [one of] the books of judiciary that the imam may appoint a successor without permission, unlike the judge, and on this his position is not vacant and deputyship is valid. And among what refutes al-Tarsusi is that al-Khassaf clarified that the caretaker may appoint an agent to stand in his place and may give him something from his salary, and likewise in al-Is'af, and this is a clear statement of the permissibility of deputizing because the deputy is a paid agent, as is not hidden. So what is established is the permissibility of deputizing in positions. If you say: Does the trustee have the authority to cut off the salary of the position-holder based solely on the statement of the attendance clerk, along with the claimant's claim of his presence? I say: I have not seen any narration from our companions on this, but Imam al-Subki mentioned in his Fatawa that it is not permissible to cut off based solely on the statement of the attendance clerk, and he stated that it is not permissible for the attendance clerk to write against him until he knows that his absence was without excuse. But this is based on his school that absence with an excuse does not cause deprivation, but according to what we have presented of non-entitlement, then no. And some rulings of positions will come in the explanation of the trustee's actions, God willing. The second topic: On the trustee by condition: We have presented that the authority of the waqf founder is fixed during his life even if he did not stipulate it, and that he has the right to dismiss the trustee, and that one he appoints does not have authority after his death except by condition according to Abu Yusuf. And if the founder appoints an executor at the time of his death and does not mention anything about the affairs of the waqf, the authority of the waqf goes to the executor, and if he makes him an executor only in the matter of the waqf, then [something]. Shaykh Khayr al-Din al-Ramli by what the author mentioned here: his statement: (And on this al-Ramli said: i.e. on the saying of impermissibility of deputizing. His statement: (The caretaker may appoint an agent etc.) al-Ramli said: The issue of the caretaker's agency will also come in the end of the explanation of this statement. And he said in his al-Khayriyya Fatawa after quoting the gist of the author's speech here: And the issue has been written about, and it is obligatory to act upon what the people practice, especially with the existence of an excuse, and on that all the salary is for the one who appointed him, and the deputy has nothing except the wage for which he hired him during the period of his deputyship, no more, and his entitlement to the wage because he fulfilled the work for which he hired him therein, and that is based on what the later scholars said, and upon it is the fatwa that hiring for imamate, teaching, and Quran instruction is permissible. End. His statement: (I have not seen a narration from our companions etc.) It has preceded that if the trustee denies his attendance, the word is the word of the teacher with his oath, and likewise if he dies and disputes with his heirs, the word is the word of the heirs with their oath, and similarly every position: the word is his word with his oath in direct performance, to the end of what we have quoted from al-Ramli in the sixth issue of the twenty issues. His statement: (We have presented) i.e. three folios earlier. His statement: (And Abu Yusuf said it is permissible) He said in Anfa' al-Wasa'il: And it should be that the fatwa is upon it, either because he adopted istihsan, and the principle is that it takes precedence over [qiyas]... [PAGE_387] ...an executor in all things according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf and Hilal. And neither of the two trustees may act without the opinion of the other. And by analogy on Abu Yusuf's saying, it is permissible. And if one of them appoints the other at the time of his death, the remaining one may act alone. And if he stipulates that the trustee should not appoint anyone at his death, appointment is prohibited. And if he makes it for two men, and one accepts and the other refuses, the judge joins to the one who accepted a man, or delegates to the one who accepted alone. And if he makes it for so-and-so until my two sons reach maturity, then when they reach maturity they become partners with him, it is not permissible what he made for his son in the narration of al-Hasan. And Abu Yusuf said it is permissible. And if he appoints a man to buy with named money land and make it a waqf, specifying it, and witnesses his will, it is permissible, and he becomes a trustee, and he may appoint another in his place. And if he appoints a trustee over his waqf, then makes another waqf and does not appoint a trustee for it, the first trustee does not become trustee over the second unless he says: you are my executor. And if he waqfs two pieces of land and appoints a trustee for each, one does not share with the other. And if he makes the authority of his waqf for a man, then makes another man his executor, he becomes a partner with the trustee in the matter of the waqf, unless he says: I have made my land a waqf for such and such, and I have made its authority for so-and-so, and I have made so-and-so an executor for my estates and all my affairs, then each one is independent in what was delegated to him; thus in al-Is'af. And from it is known the answer to a case: two documents were found, one witnessing that the trustee is so-and-so, and the other witnessing that the trustee is another man, and the second is later in date. I answered that they both share, and it is not said that the second abrogates, as al-Khassaf said in al-Shara'it, because we say: the appointment by the waqf founder is outside the ruling of other conditions, because he has the power to change and alter whenever he wishes, without a condition in the bond of the waqf according to Abu Yusuf. As for other conditions, they must be mentioned in the original waqf. Then he said in al-Is'af: And if he makes the authority for the best of his children, and they are equal in excellence, it goes to the eldest in age, male or female. And if he says 'the most excellent then the most excellent of my children', and the most excellent of them refuses to accept or dies, it goes to the one after him in excellence, and so on in order; thus mentioned by al-Khassaf. And Hilal said: Measurement requires that the judge appoint a man in his place as long as he is alive, then when he dies, the authority goes to the one after him in excellence. And if the most excellent is not capable, the judge appoints a man to manage the waqf as long as the most excellent is alive, then when he dies it transfers to the one after him in excellence. Then when he becomes capable thereafter, the authority returns to him. And similarly the ruling if none of them is capable, then the judge appoints... in addition to measurement except in issues that are not this one, and because the fatwa in waqf is on the saying of Abu Yusuf. Then he discussed that the trustee of waqf is likewise, and its completion is in it, so refer to it. His statement: (Then each one is independent in what was delegated to him) Perhaps its reasoning is that the matter of the waqf is not from the affairs of the waqf founder, so his saying 'in my estates and all my affairs' does not include it, so it was a specification of the waqf, so the first does not share, unlike the first case where the executorship was absolute, ponder. His statement: (As mentioned from al-Khassaf) i.e. five folios earlier, that if he stipulated that it not be sold, then said at the end 'on condition that he can exchange', it is permissible for him because the second abrogates the first. His statement: (And if the most excellent is not capable) i.e. not able to...
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq (a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq) deals with two main topics in the law of waqf: (1) the permissibility of deputizing in religious positions and salary entitlements, and (2) rules regarding the trustee appointed by the waqf founder (الناظر بالشرط). The author, Ibn Nujaym, begins by citing from 'Al-Khulasa' a scenario: a principal (الأصيل) who holds a religious position (like imamate or teaching) hires a deputy (النائب) and pays him a monthly salary. The question is whether the deputy is entitled to keep this salary. Ibn Nujaym states that the apparent ruling is that the deputy deserves it because this is a legitimate hire (إجارة) and he has performed the work, based on the fatwa of later scholars (المتأخرين) that hiring for imamate, teaching, and Quran instruction is permissible. However, if the principal did not work himself and the deputy worked, the position is considered vacant (شاغرة) and the trustee (الناظر) cannot pay either of them; only the judge can dismiss the principal. The practice in Cairo, however, follows a different view that deputizing is permissible and the position is not vacant. The author then notes that Imam al-Subki ruled that the trustee cannot cut the salary based solely on the attendance clerk's report; the clerk must know the absence was without excuse. But this depends on the school's position on whether absence with an excuse causes deprivation. The second topic concerns the trustee appointed by the founder's condition. The founder retains authority over the trustee during his life and can dismiss him. After the founder's death, the trustee's authority continues only if stipulated. If the founder appoints an executor (وصي) without mentioning the waqf, the executor automatically manages the waqf according to Abu Yusuf (the relied-upon view in this matter). The passage also discusses scenarios of multiple trustees, succession, and when a judge may appoint a replacement. Throughout, the author engages with intra-Hanafi differences (e.g., Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad and Hilal) and references works like al-Is'af and al-Khassaf's al-Shara'it.

Key Terms
الناظر (al-nāẓir): The trustee or administrator of a waqf, appointed either by the founder's condition or by the judge.
الاستنابة (al-istinābah): The act of appointing a deputy (نائب) to perform the duties of a position (e.g., imamate, teaching).
المتولي (al-mutawallī): The trustee or manager of a waqf, also called الناظر; the one who oversees the endowment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the principal does not work and the deputy works in a religious position, what is the ruling?
A) The deputy is entitled to the salary from the waqf.
B) The position becomes vacant, and the trustee cannot pay either.
C) The principal keeps the salary because he appointed the deputy.
D) The salary is split equally between principal and deputy.

Key Takeaway
Deputizing in religious positions is permissible with payment, and trustees must follow the founder's conditions strictly.

Joint Mutawallis: Must They Act Together?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on joint mutawallis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi dispute on joint mutawallis and apply the ruling to a scenario where one acts without the other.

Core Idea
Joint mutawallis must act jointly per Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but Abu Yusuf allows independent action.

This lesson examines a core intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the authority of multiple trustees (mutawallis) over a waqf. The question: if two are appointed jointly, can one act without the other's consent? We will study the positions of the early Hanafi authorities and see how this difference affects practical waqf management.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
Two individuals are appointed as joint mutawallis in all matters. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, neither may act without the other's opinion. Abu Yusuf and Hilal differ, permitting independent action.
The exact phrase 'وصياً في الأشياء كلها' is key — it means trusteeship in all matters.
2
Analyze the reasoning
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad view joint appointment as creating indivisible authority. Abu Yusuf and Hilal analogize each as a full agent, so each may act alone.
The text does not give explicit proof for either side; only a qiyas reference for Abu Yusuf.
3
Determine the practical consequence
Thamarah al-khilaf: Under Abu Hanifa, a unilateral action is invalid (batil). Under Abu Yusuf, it is valid (sahih).
This affects all transactions by one mutawalli without the other.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
Although not specified in this passage, later in the same source (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq), fatwa on waqf matters is generally according to Abu Yusuf's view.
Students should be aware of the hierarchy of opinion within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصياً في الأشياء كلها عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد خلافاً لأبي يوسف وهلال، وليس لأحد الناظرين التصرف بغير رأي الآخر، وعلى قياس قول أبي يوسف يجوز. ولو أوصى أحدهما الآخر عند موته كان للباقي الانفراد، ولو شرط أن لا يوصي به المتولي عند موته امتنع الإيصاء. ولو جعلها الرجلين فقبل أحدهما ورد الآخر ضم القاضي إلى من قبل رجلاً أو فوض للقابل بمفرده، ولو جعلها لفلان إلى أن يدرك ولدي فإذا أدرك كان شريكاً له لا يجوز ما جعله لابنه في رواية الحسن. وقال أبو يوسف يجوز ولو أوصى إلى رجل بأن يشتري بمال سماه أرضاً ويجعلها وقفاً سماها له وأشهد على وصيته جاز ويكون متولياً وله الإيصاء به لغيره، ولو نصب متولياً على وقفه ثم وقف وقفاً آخر ولم يجعل له متولياً لا يكون متولي الأول متولياً على الثاني إلا بأن يقول أنت وصبي. ولو وقف أرضين وجعل لكل متولياً لا يشارك أحدهما الآخر، ولو جعل ولاية وقفه لرجل ثم جعل رجلاً آخر وصيه يكون شريكاً للمتولي في أمر الوقف إلا أن يقول وقفت أرضي على كذا وكذا وجعلت ولايتها لفلان وجعلت فلاناً وصياً في تركاتي وجميع أموري، فحينئذ ينفرد كل منهما بما فوض إليه ؛ كذا في الإسعاف.
He is an executor in all matters according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf and Hilal. And neither of the two trustees may act without the opinion of the other. And on the analogy of Abu Yusuf's saying, it is permissible. And if one of them appoints the other at his death, the remaining one has sole authority. And if he stipulates that the trustee may not appoint anyone at his death, the appointment is prevented. And if he places it in the hands of two men, and one accepts and the other rejects, the judge appoints a man to the one who accepted, or delegates exclusively to the acceptor. And if he places it for so-and-so until my son grows up, and when he grows up he becomes a partner with him, what he gave to his son is not valid according to the narration of al-Hasan. And Abu Yusuf said: It is valid. And if he appoints a man to buy with a specified amount of money land and make it a waqf, specifying it for him, and he bears witness to his will, it is valid and he becomes the trustee, and he has the right to appoint someone else to it. And if he appoints a trustee over his waqf, then he makes another waqf and does not appoint a trustee for it, the first trustee does not become trustee over the second unless he says, "You are my executor." And if he makes two pieces of land as waqf and appoints a trustee for each, one does not share with the other. And if he places the authority of his waqf to a man, then makes another man his executor, he becomes a partner with the trustee in the matter of the waqf, unless he says, "I have made my land waqf for such and such, and I have placed its authority with so-and-so, and I have made so-and-so an executor in my bequests and all my affairs," then each one is independent in what was delegated to him; thus in al-Is'af.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage begins with an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the authority of multiple mutawallis (trustees) appointed over a waqf. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, when two individuals are appointed as trustees for all matters (وصياً في الأشياء كلها), neither may act independently without the other's consent. In contrast, Abu Yusuf and Hilal hold that each may act alone, based on a qiyas (analogy) that each is a full agent. The author then presents several scenarios that follow from these positions. If one trustee appoints the other at death, the survivor acts alone. If the founder stipulates that the trustee may not appoint a successor, that stipulation prevents appointment. If one of two appointed trustees rejects, the judge appoints a replacement to the one who accepted. A special case: appointing a trustee until a son matures, then the son becomes a co-trustee; in a narration from al-Hasan, the initial grant to the son is invalid, but Abu Yusuf permits it. Further scenarios explain that a trustee over one waqf does not automatically become trustee over another waqf unless explicitly stated, and separate lands with separate trustees remain independent. When a person appoints a trustee for the waqf and later makes someone else his general executor (وصي), the executor shares authority in the waqf unless the founder expressly separates the waqf authority from his other affairs. All these rulings illustrate the principle that joint trusteeship requires consensus unless the founder provides otherwise.

Key Terms
وصي (wasiy): An executor or trustee appointed to manage the affairs of a waqf or estate.
متولي (mutawalli): The administrator or trustee of a waqf, appointed by the founder or by a judge.
ولاية (wilayah): Supervisory authority over the waqf, including its maintenance, leasing, and distribution of proceeds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if two individuals are appointed as joint mutawallis (trustees) of a waqf, what is the ruling regarding their actions?
A) Each can act independently without consulting the other.
B) They must both agree before any action.
C) Only the first appointed can act; the second is merely a witness.
D) The judge must approve all actions.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi waqf law, joint mutawallis do not have independent authority according to Abu Hanifa, but the operative view (mufta bihi) is Abu Yusuf's, which permits unilateral action.

Scenarios of Trusteeship: Appointment, Rejection, and Succession
Expansion of rulings on joint trusteeship with multiple scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rulings on joint mutawallis to specific scenarios such as appointment at death, rejection by one trustee, conditional trusteeship, and separation of roles.

Core Idea
The default rule can be modified by stipulation, death appointment, or explicit separation of roles.

This lesson continues from the previous one, exploring several practical scenarios that arise when trustees are appointed over a waqf. We will see how the principles of joint authority apply when one trustee appoints the other at death, when a trustee rejects appointment, when a son becomes co-trustee upon maturity, and when a founder appoints separate trustees for different waqfs or a general executor. The key is to understand when the default rule of joint authority applies and when it is overridden.

Guided Path
1
Examine the death appointment scenario
If one trustee appoints the other at his death, the survivor acts alone. This is an exception to the rule of joint action.
The text: 'ولو أوصى أحدهما الآخر عند موته كان للباقي الانفراد'.
2
Examine the rejection scenario
If one of two appointed trustees rejects, the judge either appoints a replacement to the one who accepted or gives the acceptor full authority.
This shows that the founder's intention is fulfilled as much as possible.
3
Examine the conditional trusteeship
A trustee appointed until a son matures becomes a co-trustee with the son when the condition is met. There is a dispute about the validity of the initial appointment to the son in a narration from al-Hasan; Abu Yusuf holds it valid.
Text: 'لا يجوز ما جعله لابنه في رواية الحسن. وقال أبو يوسف يجوز'.
4
Examine separate waqfs
A trustee appointed over one waqf does not automatically become trustee over another waqf unless explicitly extended. Similarly, trustees of separate waqfs do not share authority.
This emphasizes that trusteeship is specific to the waqf named in the appointment.
5
Examine general executorship vs waqf trusteeship
If a person appoints a mutawalli for a waqf and later makes someone a general executor (وصي), the executor shares authority in the waqf unless the founder explicitly separates the roles in the declaration.
The exception: if the founder says 'I made so-and-so trustee of my waqf and so-and-so executor in my other affairs', then each is independent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصياً في الأشياء كلها عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد خلافاً لأبي يوسف وهلال، وليس لأحد الناظرين التصرف بغير رأي الآخر، وعلى قياس قول أبي يوسف يجوز. ولو أوصى أحدهما الآخر عند موته كان للباقي الانفراد، ولو شرط أن لا يوصي به المتولي عند موته امتنع الإيصاء. ولو جعلها الرجلين فقبل أحدهما ورد الآخر ضم القاضي إلى من قبل رجلاً أو فوض للقابل بمفرده، ولو جعلها لفلان إلى أن يدرك ولدي فإذا أدرك كان شريكاً له لا يجوز ما جعله لابنه في رواية الحسن. وقال أبو يوسف يجوز ولو أوصى إلى رجل بأن يشتري بمال سماه أرضاً ويجعلها وقفاً سماها له وأشهد على وصيته جاز ويكون متولياً وله الإيصاء به لغيره، ولو نصب متولياً على وقفه ثم وقف وقفاً آخر ولم يجعل له متولياً لا يكون متولي الأول متولياً على الثاني إلا بأن يقول أنت وصبي. ولو وقف أرضين وجعل لكل متولياً لا يشارك أحدهما الآخر، ولو جعل ولاية وقفه لرجل ثم جعل رجلاً آخر وصيه يكون شريكاً للمتولي في أمر الوقف إلا أن يقول وقفت أرضي على كذا وكذا وجعلت ولايتها لفلان وجعلت فلاناً وصياً في تركاتي وجميع أموري، فحينئذ ينفرد كل منهما بما فوض إليه ؛ كذا في الإسعاف.
He is an executor in all matters according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf and Hilal. And neither of the two trustees may act without the opinion of the other. And on the analogy of Abu Yusuf's saying, it is permissible. And if one of them appoints the other at his death, the remaining one has sole authority. And if he stipulates that the trustee may not appoint anyone at his death, the appointment is prevented. And if he places it in the hands of two men, and one accepts and the other rejects, the judge appoints a man to the one who accepted, or delegates exclusively to the acceptor. And if he places it for so-and-so until my son grows up, and when he grows up he becomes a partner with him, what he gave to his son is not valid according to the narration of al-Hasan. And Abu Yusuf said: It is valid. And if he appoints a man to buy with a specified amount of money land and make it a waqf, specifying it for him, and he bears witness to his will, it is valid and he becomes the trustee, and he has the right to appoint someone else to it. And if he appoints a trustee over his waqf, then he makes another waqf and does not appoint a trustee for it, the first trustee does not become trustee over the second unless he says, "You are my executor." And if he makes two pieces of land as waqf and appoints a trustee for each, one does not share with the other. And if he places the authority of his waqf to a man, then makes another man his executor, he becomes a partner with the trustee in the matter of the waqf, unless he says, "I have made my land waqf for such and such, and I have placed its authority with so-and-so, and I have made so-and-so an executor in my bequests and all my affairs," then each one is independent in what was delegated to him; thus in al-Is'af.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage begins with an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the authority of multiple mutawallis (trustees) appointed over a waqf. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, when two individuals are appointed as trustees for all matters (وصياً في الأشياء كلها), neither may act independently without the other's consent. In contrast, Abu Yusuf and Hilal hold that each may act alone, based on a qiyas (analogy) that each is a full agent. The author then presents several scenarios that follow from these positions. If one trustee appoints the other at death, the survivor acts alone. If the founder stipulates that the trustee may not appoint a successor, that stipulation prevents appointment. If one of two appointed trustees rejects, the judge appoints a replacement to the one who accepted. A special case: appointing a trustee until a son matures, then the son becomes a co-trustee; in a narration from al-Hasan, the initial grant to the son is invalid, but Abu Yusuf permits it. Further scenarios explain that a trustee over one waqf does not automatically become trustee over another waqf unless explicitly stated, and separate lands with separate trustees remain independent. When a person appoints a trustee for the waqf and later makes someone else his general executor (وصي), the executor shares authority in the waqf unless the founder expressly separates the waqf authority from his other affairs. All these rulings illustrate the principle that joint trusteeship requires consensus unless the founder provides otherwise.

Key Terms
وصي (wasiy): An executor or trustee appointed to manage the affairs of a waqf or estate.
متولي (mutawalli): The administrator or trustee of a waqf, appointed by the founder or by a judge.
ولاية (wilayah): Supervisory authority over the waqf, including its maintenance, leasing, and distribution of proceeds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a waqf founder appoints a trustee for his waqf and later appoints a general executor (وصي) for his other affairs, what is the default relationship between the two?
A) The executor has exclusive authority over the waqf.
B) The trustee has exclusive authority over the waqf, and the executor has no role.
C) The executor becomes a partner with the trustee in the waqf.
D) The trustee and executor must jointly manage the waqf.

Key Takeaway
The default rule of joint authority can be modified by specific actions such as death appointment, rejection, or explicit separation of roles in the waiver.

Conflicting Documents on the Trustee: Both Valid According to Abu Yusuf
Ruling on two conflicting documents identifying the trustee, with rational proof from Abu Yusuf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that a later document appointing a different trustee does not automatically abrogate an earlier one, and apply the rule that the founder may change the trustee at will without a condition.

Core Idea
The appointment of a trustee is not like other waqf conditions — the founder retains the right to change it at any time, even without an explicit condition.

In waqf law, changes to the terms of the endowment are strictly limited. However, the appointment of a mutawalli (trustee) is treated differently. This lesson examines a case of conflicting documents identifying the trustee, and explains why the Hanafi school considers both documents valid, allowing the trustees to share authority. The reasoning draws on the principle that tawliyah is outside the ruling of other conditions, based on the view of Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting evidence
Two documents are found: one states the trustee is Person A, the other states it is Person B, with the second dated later. What is the immediate assumption?
Many would assume the later document cancels the earlier one.
2
Recognize the initial assumption
The assumption is that the second document abrogates (nasikh) the first, as is common with conditions in legal documents. The author mentions al-Khassaf might take this view.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule about tawliyah
The author rejects abrogation here because tawliyah is exceptional. The founder has the right to change the trustee at will, even without a condition in the original waqf deed.
This is based on the view of Abu Yusuf.
4
Understand the proof
The proof is rational: the founder's authority over trustee appointment is broader than other conditions. He can change it whenever he wishes, so both appointments are valid.
No specific textual dalil is cited; it is a principle of fiqh.
5
Determine the practical outcome
Both trustees share authority as joint mutawallis. The second document does not cancel the first; instead, it confirms the founder's right to add or replace trustees.
This avoids invalidity or confusion in managing the waqf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنه يعلم جواب حادثة وجد مكتوبان شهد أحدهما بأن المتولي فلان وشهد الآخر بأن المتولي رجل غيره والثاني متأخر التاريخ، فأجبت بأنهما يشتركان ولا يقال إن الثاني ناسخ كما الخصاف في الشرائط لأنا نقول : إن التولية من الواقف خارجة عن حكم سائر الشرائط لأن له فيها التغيير والتبديل كلما بدا له من غير شرط في عقدة الوقف على قول أبي يوسف، وأما باقي الشرائط فلا بد من ذكرها في أصل الوقف.
From this is known the answer to an incident: two written documents were found, one testifying that the trustee is so-and-so, and the other testifying that the trustee is another man, and the second is later in date. I answered that they both share, and it should not be said that the second abrogates the first, as al-Khassaf in the conditions, because we say: the appointment of a trustee by the waqf founder is outside the ruling of all other conditions, because he has the right to change and replace whenever he wishes, without a condition in the waqf deed according to Abu Yusuf. As for the other conditions, they must be mentioned in the original waqf.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling derived from the principles discussed earlier. When two contradictory documents identify different mutawallis and the second is dated later, one might assume the second cancels the first (as with typical conditions). However, the author clarifies that the appointment of a mutawalli is not like other conditions of the waqf; the founder retains the right to change the trustee at will, even without stipulating such right in the original deed, according to Abu Yusuf. Therefore, both documents are valid and the trustees share authority. This is unlike other conditions (e.g. stipulations about distribution) which must be in the original deed to be binding. The reference to al-Khassaf indicates a contrast with his view on conditions in waqf deeds generally.

Key Terms
ناسخ (nasikh): A document or provision that abrogates an earlier one, as in cancelling a previous trustee appointment.
تولية (tawliyah): The act of appointing a trustee (mutawalli) for a waqf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the incident with two conflicting documents about who is the mutawalli, why can't the second document be considered an abrogation (naskh) of the first?
A) Because the second document is not authenticated.
B) Because trustee appointment is not like other conditions; the founder can change it anytime without a condition.
C) Because Abu Yusuf's view is that only the first matters.
D) Because the witnesses are unreliable.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the founder's right to change the mutawalli is unrestricted; a later document does not abrogate an earlier one but confirms the founder's ongoing authority to appoint.

Appointment Based on Virtue: Ordered Succession and the Hilal Dispute
Rules for succession when mutawalli is appointed based on virtue, with a dispute between al-Khassaf and Hilal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule for succession when a mutawalli is appointed based on virtue and evaluate Hilal's differing view.

Core Idea
A virtuous appointment creates a dynamic succession that shifts with death or incapacity, triggering judicial intervention.

When a waqf founder stipulates that the most virtuous child should be the trustee, the rules of succession depend on whether the most virtuous is alive, dead, capable, or incapable. This passage from al-Is'af presents the position of al-Khassaf and the contrasting qiyas of Hilal, highlighting a key dispute in Hanafi waqf law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Founder's Stipulation
Determine what the founder said (e.g., 'the most virtuous of my children' or 'the most virtuous, then the most virtuous') and the default when children are equal in virtue.
If equal, the eldest becomes mutawalli regardless of gender.
2
Trace Ordered Succession
When virtue varies and the most virtuous refuses or dies, the position passes to the next in virtue. This is al-Khassaf's view.
The order is fixed by virtue, not by age.
3
Contrast Hilal's Qiyas
Hilal argues that while the most virtuous is alive, the judge should appoint a substitute, and only after death does the next in line take over. This is based on analogy with other guardianships.
The disagreement concerns the timing of transition, not the ultimate heir.
4
Apply the Incapacity Scenario
If the most virtuous is incapable (ghayr mawdi'), both views agree that the judge appoints an outsider during incapacity, but they differ on whether the next in virtue becomes mutawalli after death or earlier.
Al-Khassaf: next only after death; Hilal: next might become active with oversight.
5
Note the Dynamic Nature
The founder's condition creates a dynamic succession: if virtue changes over time, the trusteeship may transfer accordingly, as elaborated in the next part of the passage.
This highlights the importance of the founder's intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال في الإسعاف : ولو جعل الولاية لأفضل أولاده وكانوا في الفضل سواء تكون لأكبرهم سناً ذكراً كان أو أنثى ولو قال الأفضل فالأفضل من أولادي فأبي أفصلهم القبول أو مات يكون لمن يليه فيه وهكذا على الترتيب ؛ كذا ذكر الخصاف. وقال هلال : القياس أن يدخل القاضي بدله رجلاً ما كان حياً فإذا مات صارت الولاية إلى الذي يليه في الفضل، ولو كان الأفضل غير موضع أقام القاضي رجلاً يقوم بأمر الوقف ما دام الأفضل حياً، فإذا مات ينتقل إلى من يليه فيه، فإذا صار أهلاً بعد ذلك ترد الولاية إليه، وهكذا الحكم لو لم يكن فيهم أحد أهلاً لها فإن القاضي يقيم أجنبياً إلى أن يصير منهم أحد أهلاً فترد إليه ولو صار المفضول من أولاده أفضل ممن كان أفضلهم تنتقل الولاية إليه بشرطه إياها لأفضلهم فينظر في كل وقت إلى أفضلهم كالوقف على الأفقر فالأفقر من ولده فإنه يعطي الأفقر منهم، وإذا صار غيره أفقر منه يعطى الثاني ويحرم الأول، ولو جعلها لاثنين من أولاده وكان فيهم ذكر وأنثى صالحين للولاية تشاركه فيها لصدق الولد عليها أيضاً بخلاف ما لو قال الرجلين من أولادي فإنه لا حق لها حينئذ. ولو جعلها لرجل ثم عند وفاته قال قد أوصيت إلى فلان ورجعت عن كل وصية لي بطلت ولاية المتولي وصارت للوصي، ولو قال رجعت عما أوصيت به ولم يوص إلى أحد ينبغي للقاضي أن يولي غيره من يوثق به لبطلان الوصية برجوعه .اهـ. ما في الإسعاف.
Then he said in al-Is'af: If he gives the authority to the most virtuous of his children and they are equal in virtue, then it goes to the eldest among them, male or female. And if he says 'the most virtuous, then the most virtuous' of my children, and the most virtuous refuses acceptance or dies, then it goes to the next in virtue, and so on in order; thus mentioned al-Khassaf. And Hilal said: The analogy is that the judge should enter a man in his place as long as he is alive, then when he dies, the authority goes to the next in virtue. And if the most virtuous is not capable (غير موضع), the judge appoints a man to manage the waqf as long as the most virtuous is alive; then when he dies, it transfers to the next in virtue; then if (the most virtuous) becomes qualified after that, the authority returns to him. Similarly, if none of them are qualified, the judge appoints an outsider until one of them becomes qualified, then it is returned to him. And if the less virtuous among his children becomes more virtuous than the one who was the most virtuous, the authority transfers to him because of the condition for the most virtuous. So he looks at every moment to the most virtuous, like the waqf for the poorest then the poorest of his children: he gives to the poorest among them, and when another becomes poorer than him, the second is given and the first is deprived. And if he places it to two of his children, and among them are a male and a female qualified for trusteeship, she shares in it because the term 'child' also applies to her, contrary to if he said 'two men' of my children, then she has no right then. And if he places it to a man, then at his death he says, 'I have appointed so-and-so and I have revoked every will of mine,' the authority of the trustee is void and becomes for the executor. And if he says, 'I have revoked what I bequeathed' and does not appoint anyone, it is incumbent on the judge to appoint another trustworthy person due to the voidness of the will by his revocation. End. This is what is in al-Is'af.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage, quoted from al-Is'af, discusses the conditions when a waqf founder stipulates that the mutawalli should be the most virtuous (afdal) among his children. Several rules follow: if all children are equal in virtue, the eldest becomes mutawalli, regardless of gender. If the founder says 'the most virtuous then the most virtuous,' the position passes in order of virtue; if the most virtuous refuses or dies, the next in line takes over. Hilal disagrees with the orderly succession: he argues that while the most virtuous lives, the judge should appoint a substitute, and only after the most virtuous's death does the next become trustee. Moreover, if the most virtuous is incapable, the judge appoints an outsider until the most virtuous becomes capable, then the authority returns. This dynamic nature is compared to a waqf for the poorest children where the recipient changes as poverty shifts. When the appointment includes both male and female children, both are eligible if the term 'children' is used; but if 'two men' is specified, females are excluded. The passage also addresses revocation: if the founder dies after appointing a mutawalli but then declares a new appointment and revokes all wills, the first mutawalli's authority ends and the new appointee takes over. If he revokes without appointing a replacement, the judge must appoint a trustworthy person.

Key Terms
الأفضل فالأفضل (al-afdal fa al-afdal): A stipulation that the mutawalli should be the most virtuous, and if he is not available, then the next most virtuous, etc.
موضع (mawdi'): Capable or qualified for the position; literally 'place' meaning fit for the role.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when the most virtuous child is incapable of managing the waqf?
A) The next most virtuous child becomes mutawalli immediately.
B) The judge appoints an outsider temporarily until the most virtuous becomes capable or dies.
C) The waqf becomes invalid.
D) The founder must be asked to appoint someone else.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school records two views on the succession of a virtuous trustee: al-Khassaf limits succession to death or refusal, while Hilal allows judicial substitution during incapacity.

Dynamic Authority, Gender Inclusion, and Revocation in Waqf Trustee Appointment
Rules on dynamic virtue transfer, female eligibility, and revocation in waqf trustee appointments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules for dynamic transfer of trusteeship due to changing virtue, determine female eligibility, and explain the effect of revocation on waqf appointments.

Core Idea
A virtuous condition makes trusteeship dynamic: authority transfers with shifts in virtue, gender inclusion turns on wording, and revocation nullifies the prior appointment.

The same passage from al-Is'af continues with three additional rules: (1) if a less virtuous child becomes more virtuous, the trusteeship transfers to him dynamically; (2) when the founder says 'children,' both males and females are eligible, but if he says 'men,' females are excluded; (3) if the founder revokes his appointment and will, the trustee's authority ends and the judge steps in. These rules demonstrate the founder's control and the flexible nature of waqf administration.

Guided Path
1
Understand Dynamic Virtue Transfer
If the founder stipulates 'for the most virtuous,' the trusteeship shifts as relative virtue changes. This is analogous to a waqf for the poorest (faqir fa-faqir) where the recipient changes when another becomes poorer.
This ensures the founder's intention is continuously fulfilled.
2
Apply Gender Inclusion Rule
When the founder uses the word 'children' (awladi), both males and females are eligible. But if he specifically says 'two men' (rajulayn), then women are excluded.
The key is the literal wording: 'child' includes daughters; 'men' does not.
3
Analyze Revocation Scenarios
If the founder, at death, appoints a new mutawalli and revokes all previous wills, the first mutawalli's authority is void. If he revokes without appointing a replacement, the judge must appoint a trustworthy person.
Revocation is effective even during the deathbed (marad al-mawt).
4
Synthesize the Founder’s Control
These rules show that the founder's stipulation governs continuously (dynamic virtue) and that he can alter or revoke the appointment before death. The judge only intervenes when the condition cannot be fulfilled.
The waqf is not static; it responds to changes in circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال في الإسعاف : ولو جعل الولاية لأفضل أولاده وكانوا في الفضل سواء تكون لأكبرهم سناً ذكراً كان أو أنثى ولو قال الأفضل فالأفضل من أولادي فأبي أفصلهم القبول أو مات يكون لمن يليه فيه وهكذا على الترتيب ؛ كذا ذكر الخصاف. وقال هلال : القياس أن يدخل القاضي بدله رجلاً ما كان حياً فإذا مات صارت الولاية إلى الذي يليه في الفضل، ولو كان الأفضل غير موضع أقام القاضي رجلاً يقوم بأمر الوقف ما دام الأفضل حياً، فإذا مات ينتقل إلى من يليه فيه، فإذا صار أهلاً بعد ذلك ترد الولاية إليه، وهكذا الحكم لو لم يكن فيهم أحد أهلاً لها فإن القاضي يقيم أجنبياً إلى أن يصير منهم أحد أهلاً فترد إليه ولو صار المفضول من أولاده أفضل ممن كان أفضلهم تنتقل الولاية إليه بشرطه إياها لأفضلهم فينظر في كل وقت إلى أفضلهم كالوقف على الأفقر فالأفقر من ولده فإنه يعطي الأفقر منهم، وإذا صار غيره أفقر منه يعطى الثاني ويحرم الأول، ولو جعلها لاثنين من أولاده وكان فيهم ذكر وأنثى صالحين للولاية تشاركه فيها لصدق الولد عليها أيضاً بخلاف ما لو قال الرجلين من أولادي فإنه لا حق لها حينئذ. ولو جعلها لرجل ثم عند وفاته قال قد أوصيت إلى فلان ورجعت عن كل وصية لي بطلت ولاية المتولي وصارت للوصي، ولو قال رجعت عما أوصيت به ولم يوص إلى أحد ينبغي للقاضي أن يولي غيره من يوثق به لبطلان الوصية برجوعه .اهـ. ما في الإسعاف.
Then he said in al-Is'af: If he gives the authority to the most virtuous of his children and they are equal in virtue, then it goes to the eldest among them, male or female. And if he says 'the most virtuous, then the most virtuous' of my children, and the most virtuous refuses acceptance or dies, then it goes to the next in virtue, and so on in order; thus mentioned al-Khassaf. And Hilal said: The analogy is that the judge should enter a man in his place as long as he is alive, then when he dies, the authority goes to the next in virtue. And if the most virtuous is not capable (غير موضع), the judge appoints a man to manage the waqf as long as the most virtuous is alive; then when he dies, it transfers to the next in virtue; then if (the most virtuous) becomes qualified after that, the authority returns to him. Similarly, if none of them are qualified, the judge appoints an outsider until one of them becomes qualified, then it is returned to him. And if the less virtuous among his children becomes more virtuous than the one who was the most virtuous, the authority transfers to him because of the condition for the most virtuous. So he looks at every moment to the most virtuous, like the waqf for the poorest then the poorest of his children: he gives to the poorest among them, and when another becomes poorer than him, the second is given and the first is deprived. And if he places it to two of his children, and among them are a male and a female qualified for trusteeship, she shares in it because the term 'child' also applies to her, contrary to if he said 'two men' of my children, then she has no right then. And if he places it to a man, then at his death he says, 'I have appointed so-and-so and I have revoked every will of mine,' the authority of the trustee is void and becomes for the executor. And if he says, 'I have revoked what I bequeathed' and does not appoint anyone, it is incumbent on the judge to appoint another trustworthy person due to the voidness of the will by his revocation. End. This is what is in al-Is'af.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage, quoted from al-Is'af, discusses the conditions when a waqf founder stipulates that the mutawalli should be the most virtuous (afdal) among his children. Several rules follow: if all children are equal in virtue, the eldest becomes mutawalli, regardless of gender. If the founder says 'the most virtuous then the most virtuous,' the position passes in order of virtue; if the most virtuous refuses or dies, the next in line takes over. Hilal disagrees with the orderly succession: he argues that while the most virtuous lives, the judge should appoint a substitute, and only after the most virtuous's death does the next become trustee. Moreover, if the most virtuous is incapable, the judge appoints an outsider until the most virtuous becomes capable, then the authority returns. This dynamic nature is compared to a waqf for the poorest children where the recipient changes as poverty shifts. When the appointment includes both male and female children, both are eligible if the term 'children' is used; but if 'two men' is specified, females are excluded. The passage also addresses revocation: if the founder dies after appointing a mutawalli but then declares a new appointment and revokes all wills, the first mutawalli's authority ends and the new appointee takes over. If he revokes without appointing a replacement, the judge must appoint a trustworthy person.

Key Terms
الأفضل فالأفضل (al-afdal fa al-afdal): A stipulation that the mutawalli should be the most virtuous, and if he is not available, then the next most virtuous, etc.
موضع (mawdi'): Capable or qualified for the position; literally 'place' meaning fit for the role.
الوقف على الأفقر فالأفقر (al-waqf 'ala al-afqar fa al-afqar): A waqf for the poorest, then the next poorest, etc., where the recipient changes as poverty levels shift.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a founder says 'two of my children' (without specifying gender), what is the ruling regarding a qualified daughter?
A) She is excluded because women cannot be mutawallis.
B) She is included because 'child' applies to her.
C) She is included only if the founder explicitly says 'daughter'.
D) She is excluded because the default is male.

Key Takeaway
The founder's condition creates a dynamic trusteeship that adapts to changing virtue, includes females when general terms are used, and can be revoked, leaving the judge to fill any vacancy.

Criteria for Choosing a Mutawalli in Waqf
Criteria for choosing among candidates for waqf trusteeship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criteria for preferring one candidate for waqf trusteeship over another, and define al-salih and al-rashid as per al-Khassaf.

Core Idea
Knowledge of waqf management outweighs extra piety when selecting a trustee.

In waqf administration, the founder often specifies conditions for the mutawalli. When multiple candidates exist, the Hanafi school provides clear rules for preference. This lesson examines those rules, emphasizing that competence (knowledge of waqf affairs) takes priority over extra piety, and clarifies the moral and financial qualifications of a suitable trustee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two comparison scenarios
The text describes two situations: (1) two candidates are equal in all virtues; (2) one is more pious, the other more knowledgeable. Note the ruling for each.
The rule is consistent: knowledge is preferred.
2
State the preference rule
When equal in deen, rectitude, virtue, and good judgment, the one more knowledgeable about waqf affairs is chosen. Even if one is more pious, knowledge still takes precedence, provided the knowledgeable candidate is trustworthy.
Trustworthiness is a condition, not just a preferred quality.
3
Understand the definitions of salih and rashid
Al-Khassaf defines salih as one who is not scandalous, not a drunkard, not a slanderer, etc. Rashid means sound management of wealth. These definitions determine eligibility.
Salih is moral integrity; rashid is financial competence.
4
Apply the criteria
Given a hypothetical pair of candidates, determine who should be appointed using the text's rule. Justify based on knowledge and trustworthiness.
Practice using the definitions to evaluate candidates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الظهيرية : إذا شرطها لأفضلهم واستوى اثنان في الديانة والسداد والفضل والرشاد فالأعلم بأمر الوقف أولى، ولو كان أحدهما أكثر ورعاً وصلاحاً والآخر أوفر علماً بأمور الوقف فالأوفر علماً أولى بعد أن يكون بحال تؤمن خيانته وعائلته، ولو جعل الولاية إلى عبد الله حتى يقدم زيد فهو كما قال، فإذا قدم زيد فكلاهما واليان عند أبي حنيفة. المتولي إذا أراد أن يفوض إلى غيره عند الموت إن كان الولاية بالإيصاء يجوز ، وإذا أراد أن يقيم غيره مقام نفسه في حياته وصحته لا يجوز إلا إذا كان التفويض إليه على سبيل التعميم اهـ فإن قلت لو شرطه للرشيد الصالح من ولده فمن يستحقه؟ قلت : فسر الخصاف الصالح بمن كان مستوراً ليس بمهتوك ولا صاحب ريبة، وكان مستقيم الطريق سليم الناحية كامن الأذى قليل السوء، ليس بمعاقر للنبيذ ولا ينادم عليه الرجال، وليس بقذاف المحصنات ولا معروفاً بالكذب، فهذا عندنا من أهل الصلاح، وكذا إذا قال من أهل العفاف أو الفضل أو الخير فالكل سواء اهـ. والظاهر أن الرشد صلاح المال وهو حسن التصرف .. الموضع الثالث في الناظر المولى من القاضي ينصبه القاضي في مواضع : الأول إذا مات التصرف في الوقف تأمل قوله : (المتولى إذا أراد أن يفوض إلى غيره (الخ) قال الطرسوسي : الذي يظهر لي أنه إنما كان كذلك لأن الوقف يبقى في حياة الواقف وبعد موته على حاله فإذا ولاه النظر بقي بالنظر إلى أنه استفاد الولاية من الواقف كالوكيل عنه فيبطل بموته، وله عزله كلما بدا له وبالنظر إلى بقاء الذي وكله لأجله بعد موته وهو الموقوف جعل كالوصي حتى كان له أن يسنده عند موته فعملنا بالشبهين وقلنا إنه ليس له أن يفوض النظر في حياته كالوكيل وعند موته قلنا له ذلك كالوصي المشابهته الوكيل من وجه والوصي من وجه . وأما قوله إلا إذا كان التفويض إليه على سبيل العموم هذا الاستناب مخصوص بالأخير وهو التفويض في حال الحياة بمعنى أنه ولاه وأقامه مقام نفسه وجعل له أن يسنده ويوصي به إلى من شاء، ففي هذه الصورة يجوز التفويض منه في حال الحياة وفي حالة المرض المتصل بالموت .
And in al-Zahiriyya: If he stipulates it for the most virtuous among them, and two are equal in religiosity, rectitude, virtue, and good judgment, then the one most knowledgeable about the waqf's affairs is preferred. And if one of them is more pious and righteous and the other has more knowledge of waqf affairs, then the one with more knowledge is preferred, provided he is in a state that his treachery and family are safe. And if he gives the authority to 'Abdullah until Zayd arrives, it is as he said; when Zayd arrives, both are trustees according to Abu Hanifa. The trustee, if he wants to delegate to another at death, if the trusteeship was by appointment (bi al-isa'), it is permissible; and if he wants to place another in his place during his lifetime and health, it is not permissible unless the delegation is on a general basis. End. If you say: If he stipulates it for the righteous (rashid salih) among his children, who deserves it? I say: Al-Khassaf explained al-salih as one who is concealed (mustawir), not scandalous nor suspicious, of upright path, sound in character, one whose harm is hidden, with little evil, not addicted to nabidh (wine) nor associating with men over it, not one who slanders chaste women nor known for lying. So this with us is from the people of righteousness. Similarly, if he says 'from the people of chastity, virtue, or goodness,' all are the same. End. And apparently, al-rashd is soundness of wealth, i.e., good management. The third section: on the overseer appointed by the judge; the judge appoints him in places: the first when the management of the waqf dies. Consider his saying: 'The trustee if he wants to delegate...' al-Tarsusi said: What appears to me is that it is because the waqf remains in the life of the founder and after his death in its state, so when he appoints him to supervision, it remains by consideration that he derived the authority from the founder as an agent, so it becomes void at his death, and he can dismiss him whenever he wishes. By consideration of the continuance of the one for whom he was appointed after his death, which is the waqf, he is made like an executor so that he can assign at his death. So we acted on both analogies and said: He may not delegate supervision in his life like an agent, and at his death we permit it like an executor, because he resembles an agent from one aspect and an executor from another. As for his saying 'unless the delegation is on a general basis,' this appointment is specific to the latter, i.e., delegation during life in the sense that he appointed him and placed him in his position and gave him the ability to assign and bequeath to whomever he wishes. So in this case, delegation is permissible from him during life and during terminal illness.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage covers several independent points drawn from al-Zahiriyya and al-Tarsusi. First, when choosing a mutawalli based on virtue, if two candidates are equal in all qualities, the one more knowledgeable about waqf management is preferred. Even if one is more pious, if the other has superior knowledge of waqf affairs, knowledge takes precedence, provided the knowledgeable person is trustworthy. This stresses competency over extra piety. Second, if the founder appoints a trustee until a specific person arrives (e.g., 'until Zayd comes'), both are trustees upon Zayd's arrival, per Abu Hanifa. Third, a trustee's power to delegate: if the trusteeship was via will (الإيصاء), he can appoint someone at his death. But during his lifetime, he cannot appoint a successor unless the original appointment explicitly granted him general authority to delegate. Al-Tarsusi explains the reasoning: the trustee is like an agent (وكيل) regarding the founder, so his authority ends at the founder's death or dismissal; but regarding the ongoing waqf, he is like an executor (وصي), so he can assign at death. The exception is if the founder gave him the right to delegate generally (على سبيل العموم), then he can delegate during life as well. Finally, the text defines 'salih' (righteous) as per al-Khassaf: a person of integrity, not openly sinful, not a drunkard, not a slanderer, not a liar. 'Rashd' means financial competence. The passage ends with an introduction to the third section on judges' appointments, but the completion is not in this window.

Key Terms
الرشيد الصالح (al-rashid al-salih): A candidate for trusteeship who is both financially competent (رشيد) and morally upright (صالح).
الأعلم بأمر الوقف (al-a'lam bi-amr al-waqf): The one most knowledgeable about waqf affairs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Greater wealth
B) More knowledge about waqf affairs
C) Older age
D) Being a male descendant

Key Takeaway
When selecting a mutawalli, Hanafi law prioritizes knowledge of waqf management over extra piety, provided the candidate is trustworthy.

Delegation of Authority by the Mutawalli: During Life and at Death
Rules of delegation by the mutawalli, with legal analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a mutawalli's delegation of authority during his lifetime vs. at death, and understand the legal analogy (shabah) that underpins the difference.

Core Idea
A mutawalli can delegate at death like an executor, but during life is like an agent who cannot delegate without permission.

The mutawalli (trustee) of a waqf may need to delegate his duties. Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between delegation at death (permissible) and delegation during life (forbidden unless the founder granted general authority). This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this distinction, using al-Tarsusi's simile of the mutawalli as both agent and executor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two delegation scenarios
The text presents two situations: (a) the trustee wishes to appoint someone after his death (at death), and (b) during his lifetime and health. Note the permissibility for each.
The default ruling: delegation at death permissible if trusteeship by will; during life impermissible.
2
Understand the legal reasoning (talil)
Al-Tarsusi explains that the trustee is like an agent (وكيل) regarding the founder: his authority is derived from the founder and can be revoked. He is like an executor (وصي) regarding the waqf: the waqf continues after death, so he can delegate at death.
The dual analogy determines the rule.
3
Identify the exception
The exception is if the founder delegated authority 'on a general basis' (على سبيل التعميم), meaning the trustee was given the right to appoint successors. In that case, lifetime delegation is permissible.
General delegation must be explicitly granted by the founder.
4
Apply the rule to new scenarios
Given a hypothetical, state whether delegation is allowed and why, using the analogy.
Practice distinguishing the two scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الشبهان (al-shabahan): The two analogies: the mutawalli is similar to an agent (وكيل) and to an executor (وصي).

Preference Among Eligible Waqf Trustees
Rulings on choosing the most qualified trustee when multiple are eligible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criteria for preferring a waqf trustee, distinguishing between knowledge and piety, and define 'righteous' (salih) and 'prudent' (rashid) as per Hanafi law.

Core Idea
Knowledge of waqf management outweighs piety in trustee selection — purpose over person.

When a waqif stipulates a condition like 'the best among them' for trustee appointment, the Hanafi school provides a clear hierarchy: the trustee most knowledgeable in waqf affairs is preferred over the more pious, as long as trustworthiness is assured. This ruling ensures the waqf's purpose is effectively served. The passage also defines key qualities and discusses delegation of trusteeship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the waqif's condition and candidates' qualities
Find the clause where the waqif sets a preference, e.g., 'the best of them'. Note the two competing qualities mentioned: piety/righteousness and knowledge of waqf affairs.
2
Compare the two candidates on piety and knowledge
The passage compares two scenarios: equal in piety and knowledge, or one more pious and the other more knowledgeable. Recognize that knowledge is preferred when piety is equal or when one is more knowledgeable but less pious (as long as trustworthy).
Key phrase: 'فالأعلم بأمر الوقف أولى'
3
Apply the Hanafi rule to decide preference
Select the more knowledgeable trustee, provided their state ensures no treachery. Understand the rationale: effective waqf management requires competence.
Condition: 'بعد أن يكون بحال تؤمن خيانته وعائلته'
4
Understand the definitions of 'righteous' and 'prudent'
Al-Khassaf defines 'righteous' (salih) by outward conduct (no flagrant sin, no bad company, etc.) and 'prudent' (rashid) as sound financial management. Apply these to determine eligibility.
Definition is practical and verifiable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الظهيرية : إذا شرطها لأفضلهم واستوى اثنان في الديانة والسداد والفضل والرشاد فالأعلم بأمر الوقف أولى، ولو كان أحدهما أكثر ورعاً وصلاحاً والآخر أوفر علماً بأمور الوقف فالأوفر علماً أولى بعد أن يكون بحال تؤمن خيانته وعائلته، ولو جعل الولاية إلى عبد الله حتى يقدم زيد فهو كما قال، فإذا قدم زيد فكلاهما واليان عند أبي حنيفة. المتولي إذا أراد أن يفوض إلى غيره عند الموت إن كان الولاية بالإيصاء يجوز ، وإذا أراد أن يقيم غيره مقام نفسه في حياته وصحته لا يجوز إلا إذا كان التفويض إليه على سبيل التعميم اهـ فإن قلت لو شرطه للرشيد الصالح من ولده فمن يستحقه؟ قلت : فسر الخصاف الصالح بمن كان مستوراً ليس بمهتوك ولا صاحب ريبة، وكان مستقيم الطريق سليم الناحية كامن الأذى قليل السوء، ليس بمعاقر للنبيذ ولا ينادم عليه الرجال، وليس بقذاف المحصنات ولا معروفاً بالكذب، فهذا عندنا من أهل الصلاح، وكذا إذا قال من أهل العفاف أو الفضل أو الخير فالكل سواء اهـ. والظاهر أن الرشد صلاح المال وهو حسن التصرف ..
In al-Zahiriyyah: If he stipulates [the trusteeship] for the best of them, and two are equal in religiosity, trustworthiness, merit, and prudence, then the most knowledgeable about waqf affairs is preferred. If one is more pious and righteous and the other more knowledgeable about waqf affairs, the more knowledgeable is preferred, provided his state is such that his treachery and family are safe. If he makes the trusteeship for Abdullah until Zayd arrives, it is as he said; when Zayd arrives, both are trustees according to Abu Hanifa. The trustee, if he wants to delegate to another at the time of death—if the trusteeship was by will, it is permissible. If he wants to appoint another in his place during his life and health, it is not permissible unless the delegation is on a general basis. If you say: If he stipulated it for the prudent and righteous among his children, who deserves it? I say: al-Khassaf interpreted 'righteous' as one who is concealed, not flagrant, not of suspicion, who is upright in path, sound in aspect, restrained in harm, little in evil, not addicted to wine nor a companion of men for it, not slandering chaste women, nor known for lying—this is, in our view, among the people of righteousness. Similarly, if he says 'from the people of chastity, merit, or good,' all are equal. And it is apparent that 'prudence' is soundness of property, which is good management.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage, from the commentary al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, collects rulings from various sources on selecting a waqf trustee when the waqif stipulated a condition like 'the best among them.' The author first cites al-Zahiriyyah on the priority of knowledge over piety in waqf management, reasoning that the purpose of the waqf is best served by administrative competence. Then he addresses delegation: a trustee appointed by will may delegate at death, but during life cannot delegate unless given general authority. Finally, he defines 'righteous' (salih) and 'prudent' (rashid) according to al-Khassaf: the righteous is one whose outward conduct is blameless, avoiding major sins and bad company; prudence is essentially financial competence. The Hanafi position is that these qualities determine eligibility.

Key Terms
الرشيد الصالح (al-rashid al-salih): The prudent and righteous person; rashid means one who manages property well, salih means one of upright conduct free from major sins.
التفويض (al-tafwid): Delegation of the trusteeship by the current trustee to another person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is preferred when two potential trustees are equally pious, but one is more knowledgeable about waqf affairs?
A) The more pious one
B) The more knowledgeable one
C) The elder one
D) The one chosen by the beneficiaries

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, knowledge of waqf management takes precedence over piety in trustee selection, as long as trustworthiness is assured, ensuring the waqf's objectives are fulfilled.

Delegation of Trusteeship (Tafwid al-Nazar) in Waqf
Ruling on trustee's power to delegate his authority to another

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a trustee (mutawalli) may delegate his authority and explain the qiyas proof (analogy to agency and executorship) that underlies it.

Core Idea
A trustee can delegate at death but not during life unless given general authority.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq clarifies the limits of a waqf trustee’s power to appoint a successor. Understanding this distinction is crucial for properly managing endowments and avoiding invalid delegations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between delegation at the time of death (if trusteeship was by will) and during life and health (only if the waqif gave general authority).
2
Trace the qiyas (analogy)
The trustee is analogized to a wakil (agent) during life (revocable) and to a wasi (executor) at death (irrevocable). This analogy determines the delegation rule.
The proof is qiyas khafi, based on the nature of the trustee's role.
3
Understand the condition for delegation during life
Delegation during life is allowed only if the waqif explicitly granted general authority ('ala sabil al-ta'mim). Otherwise, it is not permitted.
4
Examine the definition of 'righteous' and 'prudent'
Al-Khassaf defines 'salih' (righteous) with specific criteria (e.g., not a drunkard, not slandering) and 'rashid' (prudent) as sound management of property.
These definitions are used when the waqif stipulates conditions for the trustee.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical case
Consider a trustee who wants to delegate before death without general authority. The delegation is invalid. At death, if appointed by will, delegation is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المتولي إذا أراد أن يفوض إلى غيره عند الموت إن كان الولاية بالإيصاء يجوز ، وإذا أراد أن يقيم غيره مقام نفسه في حياته وصحته لا يجوز إلا إذا كان التفويض إليه على سبيل التعميم اهـ فإن قلت لو شرطه للرشيد الصالح من ولده فمن يستحقه؟ قلت : فسر الخصاف الصالح بمن كان مستوراً ليس بمهتوك ولا صاحب ريبة، وكان مستقيم الطريق سليم الناحية كامن الأذى قليل السوء، ليس بمعاقر للنبيذ ولا ينادم عليه الرجال، وليس بقذاف المحصنات ولا معروفاً بالكذب، فهذا عندنا من أهل الصلاح، وكذا إذا قال من أهل العفاف أو الفضل أو الخير فالكل سواء اهـ. والظاهر أن الرشد صلاح المال وهو حسن التصرف ..
The trustee, if he wants to delegate to another at the time of death—if the trusteeship was by will, it is permissible. If he wants to appoint another in his place during his life and health, it is not permissible unless the delegation is on a general basis. If you say: If he stipulated it for the prudent and righteous among his children, who deserves it? I say: al-Khassaf interpreted 'righteous' as one who is concealed, not flagrant, not of suspicion, who is upright in path, sound in aspect, restrained in harm, little in evil, not addicted to wine nor a companion of men for it, not slandering chaste women, nor known for lying—this is, in our view, among the people of righteousness. Similarly, if he says 'from the people of chastity, merit, or good,' all are equal. And it is apparent that 'prudence' is soundness of property, which is good management.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the trustee's (mutawalli) power to delegate his authority. The ruling distinguishes two scenarios: (1) At the time of death, if the trustee was appointed by a will (i.e., by the waqif's last testament), he may delegate to another person. (2) During his lifetime and health, he cannot do so unless the original appointment gave him general authority to delegate. The reasoning, as explained earlier in the text, is that the trustee is like an agent (wakil) during life (since the waqif can revoke), but like an executor (wasi) at death (since the waqf continues). Thus the law gives him the power to appoint a successor at death but not during life without express permission. The passage then defines 'righteous' and 'prudent' for eligibility.

Key Terms
التفويض (al-tafwid): Delegation of the trusteeship by the current trustee to another person.
المتولي (al-mutawalli): The trustee appointed to manage a waqf.
الإيصاء (al-isa'): Appointment by will (wasiyyah).
الصالح (al-salih): Righteous person, as defined by al-Khassaf (discreet, not flagrant, etc.).
الرشيد (al-rashid): Prudent person, meaning one who manages property well.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition may a trustee delegate his authority during his lifetime?
A) At any time if he is competent.
B) Only if the waqif gave general authority to delegate.
C) Only when he is about to die.
D) He can never delegate.

Key Takeaway
A waqf trustee may delegate at death (if appointed by will) but during life only with the waqif's general authorization; the analogy to agency (wakalah) and executorship (wasiyyah) determines the rule.
